Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	Of these there is a way such that you make three cauteries, or four, by lining according to the length of the mouse, according to the figure of the cautery of the liver that we have said before; and do not press your hand at all along the cautery, and let the patient be careful on his back; and another way of cautery is such that you heat the cautery which has two nerves, as we have shown in the dislocation of the shoulder; and lift the heart which is in the place of the mouse, or the sides of the disease come towards the left, and let the elevations by which you lift the heart be according to the heart, according to the length of the body, and the cauteries be according to the breadth of the body.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	Afterwards, I put the two nerves into the flame until the heart is pierced on the other side, and then pull away the cautery; and thus there will be four of them. And if you wish, you can cauterize all along the cautery with three nerves.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the wound has healed and scabs formed for a long time, it is better than the other wounds mentioned before.
de ydropisie	of dropsy
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization does not work on syphilis, except in the manner called "asclytes.
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat it according to the methods we have described in detail, and your treatment does not help, then you should perform three cauterizations around the navel, one on the stomach, one on the liver, one on the groin, two on the back near the spine, and one on the buttocks; the cauterization should be close to the bone.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les .ij. ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	Afterward, let the cautery open to drain pus for a long time, and do not leave the treatment of the wound after the cautery; and healing will hasten, and the two intentions will be together with God's help.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the cautery for the belly should be the key that we have shown before; and that for the back should be olive-shaped, according to what is shown there before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the swelling of the feet
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the feet of one with syphilis are swollen and filled with yellow water, you should cauterize between the little toe and ring finger on the top of the foot; move your hand with the cautery without turning it.Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.

Aprés fai sus .ij. jambes .ij. cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit. de la menoison	of the moon
Quant solution de ventre vient de froidor et de moistor, tant que li vertus retentive et digestive qui est ou stomac et en l’intestine est afleboie, et ne puet estre curez par manieres de cures; et tu vois le malaide bien soffrant et de fort vertut, si fai .i. grant cautere sus l’estomac selonc ceu qu’il en a parleit ci devant ou cautere de l’estomac, au cautere circule; et .iiij. cauteres entor la boude subtilz a tout .i. cautere clavile subtil, et .ij. cauteres sus les hainches.	When diarrhea comes from cold and moisture, and the retentive and digestive powers in the stomach and intestines are weakened, and cannot be cured by usual means; and you see the patient suffering greatly and very weak, then make one large cautery on the stomach according to what was described earlier for the stomach cautery, and four small cauteries around the navel, one cautery clavicle below the navel, and two cauteries on the hips.
Et se tu vois les moistors habundans et le malaide soffrant, se li fai cautere sus le poignil, et .i. cautere sus chaicun yle, et .ij. petis cauteres sus l’estomac delez le grant, car li cure est profitans quant il i a bone aide.	And if you see the patient suffering from abundant moisture, make a cautery on the wrist, and one cautery on each elbow, and two small cauteries on the stomach below the large one, for the cautery is beneficial when there is good circulation.Et si li est trop de moistors, et tu vois li sang en isse par la ventrez, fai l’incision sus la ventrez par le mi-cau, car si li sang est de la ventrez et non de la veine, il ne sera pas mist, et li malaide soit mort.
de la cure des emorroydes	of the treatment of hemorrhoids
Quant les emorroydes sont ou fondement, ou une ou plusors, et sont ancienes et sont de grosses humors froides et moistes corrumpues, et sont curees si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie, si fai cauteres: III sus l’espine dou dos, celi qui est tout defuers desoz almecdate poc et poc en triangulant, et I cautere desoz la boude II dois; et se tu penses que ses estomac soit refroidiez, et li viande ne cuise, et on voit enfler la faice, adonques li faice on I grant cautere sus le stomac, si com il est devant dit, et I autre sus le foie, et I autre sus la mice a tout le cautere clavile; et laisse le cautere overt lonc tens.	When the hemorrhoids are in the anus, one or more, and are old and consist of thick cold moist corrupt humors, and are treated as we have described in divisions, and it does no good, then make cauteries: three on the spine of the back, that which is completely outside below the armpit in a triangle, and cauterize underneath the jawbone two times; and if you think his stomach is cooled, and the meat doesn't cook, and one sees the face swell, then cauterize the face greatly over the stomach, as was previously described, and the other over the liver, and the other over the mouse with the full cautery of a key; and leave the cautery uncovered for a long time.

de la charnositeit qui est nommee «thelul»	of the fleshy growth called "thelul"
Quant tu copes althelul, si eschaufe le cautere qui semble .i. raseur, et puis le met tout embraseit sus cel althelul copeit; et i laisse tant ta main que li cauteres viegne a la naissance de la voine, de coi li sans cort; fai ceu une fois ou .ij., et s’il i a mout d’althelul, si cauterize chaicun si com nos avons dit; aprés les cure d’oignemens profitans tant qu’il soient sanez; et se tu cauterizes d’un cautere grant sus alchatim, si avra plus grant aide.	When you apply the cautery, heat it until it looks like a razor, and then place it directly on the shaven skin; hold your hand so that the cautery reaches the vein's opening, from which the blood flows; do this once or twice, and if there is a lot of skin, cauterize each one as we have said; after this, treat the wound with healing ointments until they are healed; and if you cauterize with a large cautery on the scrotum, it will provide greater relief.
de plaie mal curee	from wounds that were not properly treated
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot tolerate cutting or opening, as we will describe in its place, then such a disease comes that it cannot be healed except by cautery.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When a person has a fistula, and it is suppurating and oozing pus and corrupted moisture, then you must test it with a thin needle, and be careful that you know how deep the needle goes.
Aprés eschaufe le cautere qui semble I raseur, et le boute en la fistule selonc la quantiteit que li tente i est entrée, et rencomence lou cautere tant que cil cors porris et corrumpus soient ars, une fois, ou II ou III, selonc la quantiteit de som besoing; et te warde d’ardre lé nerf qui sunt enqui, et des grans voinnes.	After heat the cautery which looks like a razor, and insert it into the fistula according to the amount that the needle entered, and repeat the cautery until the pus and corruption are burned, once, or twice or thrice, according to the amount needed; and be wary of burning the nerves that are nearby, and large veins.
se li fistule vait au cors de la vesie et a l’intestine, si te warde de ces leus, et ne faire ceu fuers que en leu charnut, et pense qu’ele n’est mie persans; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez, et se li leus est saielez, et les matieres sont ostees lonc tens, adonc saiches que li leus est sanez entierement; et se les matieres ne sont ostees, saiche que li leus est troez, et corrumpus li os au font; et ensi com un de ces que nos dirons en son leu.	if the fistula goes into the bladder and intestine, then be wary of those areas, and only do this on fleshy areas, and think that it is not painful; after curing the area until it is healed, and if the area is swollen and the matter is not expelled for a long time, then know that the area is completely healed; and if the matter is not expelled, know that the joint is broken, and the bone at the bottom is damaged; and thus as one of those we will say in their place.
de la maladie des reins	of kidney disease

de la vessie	of the bladder

de la marris	of diseases
Quant li marrix est froide et moiste, et ne laisse mie por ceu a concevoir, et les flors sont corrumpues et lor termines tarde; et quant elles vienent, si sent grant dolor: adonques covient il c’on li faice .iij. cauteres entor la boude, si com nos avons dit ou cautere de la vessie, et .ij. cauteres defuers le dos; et soit li cauteres clavile, si com nos avons dit. de la hainche	of the hip
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a .i. cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moistors descend to the box of the hip, and due to this they move out of their place, and the sign is that the thigh is longer than the other when measured together; and it is found that the places of the departure are hollow, then one should cauterize the patient on the box of the hip with 1 cautery resembling a circle, and sign before the place around the box as it turns, so that the box is within the circle; and let the cautery be like those by which one has cauterized the stomach.
Et se cist cauteres ne t’est presens, se li fai .iij. cauteres de l’olivaire grans, et soit li cauteres ausi parfont com tous li keurs; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if this cautery is not available to you, then make three large cauteries from the olive tree, and let the cauteries be as deep as all the sores; and treat it until it is healed.
de la dolor de la hainche	of the pain in the hip
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain arises in the hip joint due to cold and moisture, and the disease is chronic and resistant to the treatments mentioned earlier, then you must purge the patient of the gross humours with foul-smelling pills or similar good pills.
Aprés li fai cautere; et li maniere dou cautere si est selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir ensamble medicines ardans, et cautere de feu.	After him, let them cauterize it; and there are two ways of cauterization: one is with burning remedies, the other with fire.
Cautere de feu si est selonc mout de manieres, desquelz li uns est telz: que tu cauterize sus la boiste de la hainche III cauteres triangulalz selonc ceste forme, et i fai bone profunditeit et grant, et ait entre chaicun cautere d’espaice la groissece d’un doi, et soit li cauteres olivaire; aucune fois fait on cautere en mileu sus lou chief de la hainche, por coi il en i a IIII selonc ceste forme:	Fire cauterization has many methods, one of which is as follows: make three triangular cauteries on the pelvis according to this shape, and make them deep and large, with a distance of a thumb between each cautery; sometimes a cautery is made in the middle of the hip, so that there are four according to this shape.
Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if you see, the cautery with the circular cauterizer that we have mentioned before in the dislocation of the hip; but do it in such a way that the circles contain the entire hip, and all the thickness of the skin is burned.
Et c’est li maniere c’on fait en sciatique, quant li dolor tient en la hainche, et ne parvient mie jusc’a la cuisse ne jusc’a la jambe.	And this is the way it is done in sciatica when the pain stays in the hip and does not go down to the thigh or leg.
Et s’ele vient jusc’a la cuisse et la jambe, se li fai II cauteres lai ou li malaides dit que li dolor li tient, et I cautere desus la cheville IIII dois, a la partie senestre un poc; et soit li cauteres cutellaire, et soit arse li espesseté dou keur; et se li malaides sent que li dolor s’estende jusc’a dois dou piet ou pres d’enqui, se le cauterize la ou il sent la dolor III poins ou IIII au cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if it extends to the leg or foot, they cauterize where he feels the pain in two or three places with what is called a 'point' cautery. And if the pain spreads to the big toe or near it, they cauterize where he feels the pain, three points or four, on the left side of the ankle; and it should be cutillary cautery, and burn the thickness of the skin; and if the patient feels that the pain extends to two of the foot, they cauterize where he feels the pain in three points with what is called a 'point' cautery.
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, make more; and if he feels that the pain is below the knee towards the thigh, make the cautery with a knife or circularly, and take good care in all your cauteries not to leave the cautery on so long that you burn the nerves and large arteries, and do not cause the patient greater harm and contraction.
Et je meisme ai veus plusors qui ont fait cautere sus la cheville dou piet, et li lasserent tant que li jambe fut toute enflee, et li piez ausi, et fut perciez et corrumpus toz li piez.	And I myself have seen many who had cautery applied to the ankle of the foot, and they left it so that the leg was completely swollen, and the foot as well, and it was pierced and corrupted throughout the foot.

And if the pain is in two parts together, apply cautery in one and then the other, according to this method.Si li poilz sont grans et lons sus les guiles qui sont pres de la cheville dou piet, et qu’il fuille par eu sang, fai li cautere sus li guiles pour qu’il ne puet demorer en li guiles, car il fuille le sang.
Et li saige dirent en la cautere de la hainche, de coi ci est li maniere, fai I tel fer et soit au chief ausi gros com uns nauvillon de dacte, ou un poc moins, et soit par entrechetres et soit des l’un entrechetres jusc’a l’autre d’espaice la quantiteit d’un nou de poce; et soient li entrechetres aovers de II pars, et soient aussi comme noez, et i ait I mainche de fer bien fait; et c’est li forme:	And if the hairs are large and long on the shins which are near the ankle of the foot, and blood flows from them, apply cautery to the shins so that it cannot remain in the shins, because blood flows from them. Et soit eschaufez tant qu’il soit toz rouges et giete senteles, et puis le mette on sus la boiste de la hainche malaide, et soit tornez sus lou sain costeit; et lou cauterize une fois .i. cautere reont et lou laisse .iij. jors; et puis fai emplaustre de burre, et laisse la plaie aoverte lonc tens; aprés la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez. Albucasim says that we use little of this cautery because of the fear of its sight, and we see few who use it; and yet it is one of the good cauteries, which those who can bear it should use where it is needed.
Li cauteres de medicine ardant si est que tu faices I estrument a entrechetres en coi dessende li marge de la porte, et soit d’arain ou de fer a une paroit longe, et en la hautece ait II nous, et ait entre chaicun la quantiteit de la groissece d’un doi; et soient overt defuer et desus, et se joignent ensamble selonc ceste forme:	The cautery of medicine burns if you make the instrument to interlace in such a way that the edge of the door descends, and it is made of brass or iron with one side long, and in the height it has two knobs, and between each knob there is the thickness of a thumb; and they are open at the bottom and above, and join together according to this form:
Aprés met sus la boiste de la hainche au malaide gisant sor suin costeit sain, et apresse ta main mout sus la boiste de la hainche; aprés giete entre les II cercles de l’awe chaude qui soit chaufee au feu I poc, et li laisse une houre dou tens, et soffre li malaides la chalor et l’arsure de li. Car il i trueve mordication ausi com de feu; et quant li mordications iert passee, se lieve ta main avec l’estrument et leve la hainche d’awe douce, et laisse ensi III jors, et met sus burre tant que ceu qui est noir de l’eschaudure soit osteit; et lou laisse III jors que porriture en istrait; et ceu serait li derriene aide aprés le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez. And if the pain has spread to the thigh or leg, do to them the instrument that dyes in salt according to what you did in the hip joint; and this is how hot salt is made, and I wrote it down in the treatise on the rectification of medicine.

Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés.	And Galen tells us of a cure by which a man was cured of pain in the hip and sciatica, and he praised it highly, saying that no other treatment was used, and that he was cured in a single session when this cure was performed, and then he bathed as he instructs below.
Et dist en teil maniere que tu preignes dou litargire vert fres et sec, et le broie mout avec I poc de graisse, et met sus la hainche et sus la cuisse et sus la jambe ou la dolor tient, et la lie; et li laisse III houres et par la quantiteit que li malaides ne sente plus l’arsure. Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with goat's dung, it helps a lot; and the cautery must be done in such a way:
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take wool and grease it with old oil, and place it on the hollow between the big toe and the one next to it, which is called the Fossette.
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	After that, take dried goat's dung and heat it in the fire until it turns into charcoal, and place it on the wool, leaving it until it burns out; do this repeatedly, and don't stop doing so until you feel through sensation that it has reached the hip and the pain has stopped; and this method of cautery is called "goat cautery.
de la dolor dou dos	of pain in the back
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes in the back, from sitting or impact or from excessive evacuation, or by similar appearances of cold matter, none of these appearances are worth cauterizing except for that which comes from the diffusion of cold matter.

Many times this disease comes to young children, and the signs of its onset are that they have a tight back when they wake up, and fear; and you find it in the last vertebrae of the back, and in us it appears on the other vertebrae.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see one and see it treated, then cauterize it with a cautery of celery according to this form.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	So that the cautery purple stains each part of the spine evenly.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see, cauterize around the spine with a pointed cautery two or three lines apart, and have the points close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	Afterwards, heal the site until it is healed according to what we have said, and be careful not to use cautery on any part that is swollen and in the swelling of a nerve.
de la dolor des jointes	of joint pain
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pains are from moistors that are spread throughout the body's limbs, and when pain comes in the feet, which they properly call "podagra," and when it is from a cold cause and cannot be cured by medicine, then it is cured by cauteries in this way: make the mouth of the cautery around the joint of the foot, and let the cautery be olive-colored according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if there is a need to prick on the sole of the foot, do cautery with the whole cautery that one calls «point.»
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if the pains come up to the knees and other joints, and this happens many times, do cautery on each knee with three or four cauteries in each part, with the whole olive cautery; and if you need more, then do more, but do not hold your hand there any longer than until the skin of the heart is burned.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend to the knee and back, administer the cautery we have described in his chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are in the hands, make a point around the wrist two lines; and if there is no more pain in the arms, make a point on each joint and on the palm of the hand; and if the pains come to the armpits or shoulders, cauterize each part, and make good management for the sick person and take medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you give him good care and purge the phlegm, he will be healed with God's help.
de la routure dou syfac	of the rot of the scrotum
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the ulcer comes in wounds, and the bowels descend to the testicles and it is new, then when you see him being treated, he should not eat that day; and he should use things that loosen the belly so that the farts descend from his belly; then make him sit on his back between your hands, and command him to hold his armpits so that the bowels are repaired, and bring them back to your fingers, and sign with ointment underneath the ulcer on the bone of the wrist, and throughout a sign that is similar to half a circle on top of the body; then heat the cautery from which this form comes:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	until it becomes white and oozes pus.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then reset the bones to their place; and have the patient keep his hand under so that they do not return; and work well into the thighs of the sick person, and put a pillow under the thighs and a servant on top of them, and another on the feet pressing down with hands; then put the cautery over the wound all the way to your fingertips, and hold it straight and hold it until you reach the bone, and if you do not reach it the first time, do it again until you reach the bone; and be careful that the pus does not leak out when you do the cautery so that you do not burn him; and through this the sick person will not die, or become worse.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And know that when you do not come to the bone with the cautery, your work is worth nothing.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cautery for children be subtle according to the size of their ears, and for large people as large according to their size; after three days, treat the site of the cautery with butter until the scorching is healed; then treat it with other ointments until it is healed, and let the patient lie on his back for forty days so that the wound is well closed; and it is necessary to let their hair grow long enough that it covers their neck when they lower their head.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wants to get up, if a well-made brace is provided for him and worn for another forty days, and he has good rest, eats and drinks little, and avoids excessive laughter, then he will be completely healed.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say hereafter about the cure for cutting in his scrotum.
de la routure dou ventre	of the bowels
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ulcers come in other bellies and are known, and you see that they are not growing, then do the cautery with the fire according to its quantity, and burn the third part of the skin; after the cure according to what we have said; and some of the ancients say that one should cauterize it with a three-pointed cautery according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first mark the place of entry and make a line across the width above the ulcer, and another across it, and hold your hand steady throughout the cautery.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first cauteries are lighter and gentler.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	of old pain in any limb
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes in a limb, from falling or injury, and the pain lasts a long time, and medicine does not help, then it should be cauterized with a cautery called 'sharp point', and the cautery should be according to the length of the limb, its thinness and weakness, and its position of twisting and pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is healed by the first cautery, that is good; if not, do another cautery on it, for such is the custom that it should move in the member nearest to it, therefore you must do the cauteries until the patient is healed.
de meselerie	from mixing
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	Sometimes ulcers are helped by cautery with great ease, especially those diseases that come from the putrefaction of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	When you see her cauterized, take care that the disease is in its early stages, and if it is cured according to what we have said in the division, and does not stop or persist, and you doubt that the corruption may spread throughout the disease, then do five cauteries on the head: one in the middle of the forehead, and one towards the front at the end of the hairline; two on the temples, and one behind on the nape of the neck; and let your hand remain so that the cautery comes to the bone, and so that the vapors of the gross humors can issue forth; and cauterize the mouse according to how it appears beforehand.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the mixing is scattered everywhere and it is manifestly losing, then you should cauterize it with those cauteries that we have said on the head, and one cautery in the navel, and two cauteries on the spine of the neck, and 6 cauteries on the spine of the back, and one large one on the hip and another one next to it, and two on the shoulders; and two on the elbows, and two on the tendons of the feet, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the hollows of the hands; and be careful of the nerves that are on the lower calf bone, so that you do not burn them; and sometimes do a cautery on the bone of the wrist, and another one on the stomach bone, and one on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And know that the more you do of cautery, the more it helps, and moves the profit; and know that the sick person does not feel pain from cautery as a healthy person feels it, because the body is already completely corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauteries be large and small according to the members and the joints, according to what you will find in the ways of the irons.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	Afterwards, treat the place with wheat flour mixed with honey and other remedies until it is healed.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes to a member and is treated with remedies, oils, and plasters but is not healed, then do cauteries on the member according to the size of the member; let the cautery be somewhat deep in the thickness of the skin; then cure it with ointments until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And sometimes cautery is done on the hand and foot and back, at the exit of the nerve that paralyzes the limb, and thus the swelling is removed; and nevertheless, no one should attempt this unless they are knowledgeable about the limbs and the exits of the nerves moving through the body.
de albaras	of albars
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is awakened, and the remedies of medicine are of no avail, then cauterize it with a cautery slightly deep, according to the quantity of the thickness of the skin, so that the whiteness is removed, and its color changed; then cure with flour of beans and lentils, with rose oil and plantain leaves, and blood of colon and blood of almond, of each one part; and mix all together, and tie it with a cloth, and air in the location until it is healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	the cure for cancer by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a ulcer comes at first, and you see it stopping, then cauterize it with the cautery that looks like a circle, all around the edge of the ulcer.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And yet the wise say that one should also do cautery in the middle of the ulcer; and yet this does not seem good to me, for I fear it will be burned and corrupted, and I have indeed seen this happen sometimes; and a more certain thing is that it be cauterized around the edge, with the cautery called the 'circle', as we have said in many cauteries.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling which cannot be cured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it is slow to die, either due to the excess that it causes or due to old age, when he is decrepit (that is, very old), and he has little blood, or because of time; and you see him hastening to die: then cauterize around with many small cauteries by pricking; afterwards leave it thus.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will hasten to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see him piercing throughout the cautery, then heat the cautery tool of which this is the shape:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of that disease which is called  "adubelati" as long as the cauteries have pierced the skin, and let the cauteries be such that the patient feels them piercing through in such a way that the flow of the pus is relieved.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterwards, treat the wound until it is perfectly healed.Et se li cauteres ne porroient pas percer li keur, tu le mets en tel maniere que li cauteres fieent entor la maladie, et les fies tout entor si com te plait a tu, car ele est resuivee par toua.
li cure dou feu par fer	the fire cure by iron
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another type of disease is called "corroding", and it is nothing other than a melting of the limbs, for it melts the limbs just as fire melts dry wood.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in a place that can withstand fire cautery, then heat the cautery needles both small and large, according to what is needed for the site of the disease; after cauterizing it all over, until you reach all the corruption, and none remains, so that all that is corrupted is removed.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and apply soft bandages soaked in oil over the cauterized areas until the burns from the fire are healed, and all the corruption is removed.Et si li membre est corrodé a la fesse ou en alte parie del corps, il faut que tu le cauterises adonques et que tu le broies avec oile selonc la quantite de la maladie; et s’il est granz et pesans, si met sur les leus cauterizez soffres broitz a la maniere susdite.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of ulcers caused by cautery.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if you see after 3 days that a healthy blister has not formed, it is good; and if not, then restart the cautery on what remains of the infected area.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this wound is sometimes cured by a medicine blister instead of fire cautery; but nonetheless, fire cautery is of greater help, and I have already described the cure for medicine blisters in the section on ulcers: take it whenever you need it.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	of warts that come on the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times, a condition called "clos" occurs on the feet due to excess moisture, and it is a large, faulty growth that blisters the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And there are two ways to perform cautery for this condition.La Iere est que tu prennes lou piet et le rases tres bien sus l’esgouttoir, et que tu esgouttes la pluitier; et que apres la rasura tu mettes une pierre chaude sus la pluitier qui soit tres chaude, et fasse que li piez se desset.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	This is to know fire cautery, and hot water cautery.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Fire cautery is when you heat the cautery iron as hot as a pen, and it is made of good steel to the size that it can touch the nail all around, and it has thin edges; after that, put it all hot on the nail, and turn your hand all around the nail until it reaches the bottom of the nail; then let it be thus for three days until it begins to form pus; then make a poultice of wild mallows, crushed with salt, and leave the poultice on all night; the nail will drop off and be uprooted by its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then cure the place with ointment until it is healed.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted to the body by defecation, and many times they happen in hands and feet, then you should administer hot water cautery; and it is in such a way: take a brass or iron rod, or a pen, and put it on the nail and the althelul, that is, warts; and place the rod on so that it blisters all around, then pour a little boiling water on it, and hold your hand steady, and press your hand as you turn so that the edge of the rod reaches the root of the nail, and can find the hot water a deep way to the root; and let the patient endure the biting of the hot water for an hour; then leave it thus, and it will be uprooted at all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	Thus do one after another, until you have extracted all those who are in the body; then clean the wounds that generate pus.
li cure dou trembler	the cure for trembling
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some people tremble from coldness of the nerves, or from quartan fever, or from other causes, then you should do four cauteries, or four on each side of the spine, one cautery between each vertebrae; and one cautery on the foot, and one on the stomach with an olive-shaped cautery; thus it will cease the trembling, and hasten the healing from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	of foul pustules
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Sometimes they appear on the surface of the body as bad-smelling boils or pustules that come from putrid matter.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If necessary, when they first appear, a cautery should be applied to the top of each pustule: a thin cautery made from a twig of myrrh, whose tip is heated, or a long root of aristolochia, or with the lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And sometimes they are cauterized at the beginning when they appear, in this way, and they cannot grow further, but the surplus from which they come is disrupted, and they become healthy; but it must be done after the evacuation of blood.Et si il appert des enquis, qu’il doit avoir l'un de chescune partie de la pustule, si convient que li cauterize soit fait en telle maniere: si adonques on le veult faire a la fust de mirte ou aristologe, si prenne la pustule et le fust en sa main, et le tienne près du feu selonc qu’il doit; et tant qu’il soit chaud, le prenne et le mette sus li chef de la pustule, et le tienne ainsi qu’il ne se remue jusqu’a ce que il le veult faire.
quant li artere est copee	when the artery is cut
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	Many times there are great discharges of blood from the artery that is cut at the wound that comes to the surface, or at the incision of an abscess, or at the cautery of a limb, and similar things; and it is a very grievous thing to stop.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And yet, when this happens to someone, you should quickly put your index finger over the wound of the vein and squeeze it hard until the blood is calmed under your finger and no drops come out; then put in the fire olive-wood cauteries, both small and large, as many as are needed, until they are all red; then take .i., either a large or small one according to the wound and where the artery is running, and put the cautery on that vein where you are holding your finger, and hold it there until the bleeding is stopped.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it bleeds again when you lift your finger off the wound, and the cautery is extinguished, then quickly take another of the cauteries which are in the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not cease to do this with one after the other until the bleeding is stopped; and beware that you do not burn the nerve which is nearby, and that no other harm comes to the patient; and know that when blood flows from an artery, it cannot be well-stopped immediately if the artery is large, except by one of four methods which we have described: either by cautery, or by extraction when it has not been treated, or by strong binding with thread, or by medicines placed on it which have the power to stop bleeding; and it should be bound and compressed skillfully.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever applies a tight binding with bandages or placing hot things on it, or other similar things, if it does not help then it is no good.Et quant li sans decourt d’une artere qui est petite, et que ne pooit mie estre restenchiee de nule maniere qui nos avons dit, si covient que l’on le fie par medicines qui ont pooir de restenchir; et si le sans decourt d’une artere grasse, si doit il estre restenchiz par liement ou par cautere.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and they do not have any mirth or present medicine, then one should place their index finger on the wound of the vein as we have said, and firmly press until it is constricted above the wound and above the vein; and one should not move it, but moisten it with cold water often so that it is very cold until the blood is congealed and swelled and constricted; and make inquiries beforehand about what they need in terms of cautery and medicine.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here begins the second book of treatments for wounds:
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	We have told you in the first chapter about every disease that requires cauterization by fire, or burning medicine, and the poultices, causes, instruments, forms of cauteries; and I have covered that chapter from head to foot, and I will continue on the same path in this chapter so that one can more easily find what they are looking for.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And so that I begin this, it is necessary, dear son, that you understand that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first one about cauteries, and therefore one must be more cautious. Car li perils et li paors que on encuntre por les tailles de s’estomache, et les maux que il en advient, si com est la piere, et l’estracions d’elle, et les saings et les maux qu’on encuntre, et les estrumens qui conviennent, et les cauteres.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you not to embark on foolishness.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many kinds of people come for treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	Some come with diseases that they will easily die of due to the foolishness they display regarding their illnesses, and because of the great severity of their conditions; one must be afraid of these people.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And there are those who give you their opinion and say, "wait, I am healed"; but the disease is stubborn.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	You should not listen to those who approach you with such an attitude, but instead place more importance on your honor than on your desires. Do not act foolishly but wisely, based on what you know and can prove, and use prognosticating and diagnosis in treating your illnesses so that salvation may be found. This will help you gain a good reputation, glory, and praise.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, may Our Lord give you wisdom and righteousness, and if you wish to be inspired by the holy breath from his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Here I have ordered this chapter in discussing by chapters, according to what it is before the chapter of cauteries, which I have discussed from the head to the feet, so that you may more easily find what you need.
dou chief plein d’aigue	from the head full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	Do you know that this disease often comes to children when they are born, and when the head is squeezed too hard during childbirth; and sometimes it comes from an unknown cause.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease in adults, and in all those that I have seen, death has followed; and because of this, it seems better to me to leave the treatment out of such cases.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw a child whose head was filled with water, and his skull grew larger every day until he could no longer support it; and he believed that the moisture would kill him, and this moisture is gathered beneath the bone above the brain, between the heart and the bone; and the treatment is such that if the moisture is between the heart and the bone, and the abscesses are small, you should split a large opening in the middle of the skull; and it should be as long as two fingers, so that the moisture runs out; and see the form of spatumile:
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper, and the abscesses are larger, then make two slits in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	And if the moisture is beneath the bone, and the signs that you see are the openings of the skull on each side, and the water jumps out when you press it with your hand from within, and it has not closed again: then you should split the skull in three places according to this manner:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, extract all the moisture forcefully.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	Afterwards, tightly bind the cuts with bandages and powders, and apply wine and oil, and leave it thus for five days; then loosen it, and treat the wound by tenting and ointments, and let the head be extracted equally, and give the patient dry meat to eat, removing moisture from the pouch until the limb is comforted and healed.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	And another way of incision is that you look at where the abscess opens, and the gathering of fluid; for sometimes it is in front, sometimes behind, sometimes on the right, and sometimes on the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	So cut where the abscess opens, and the gathering of fluid, and do it according to what you are able; and be careful not to cover the artery; and let blood flow, so that the patient dies from blood loss and the evacuation of moisture.
de reume	of gout
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When it happens to someone that they have a disease called "cataract" in their eyes or feet, and the disease is old, and medical treatment does not help, then the last resort is cauterization with which one will cut open the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	Therefore, when you see them bent, have the patient lean back; then rub the area around an artery with a rough cloth until it appears, then tightly bind the neck of the patient with the entire cloth; then examine where the vein beats, and the locations of both are after the ears, and the pouches are pushed back; then mark the locations with ink, then bandage one and the other with a sharp spatulum in two parts, so that the incision reaches the bone, and this should be done widely from the back of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	And if you see it, tie the bandage under the artery and over it, cutting also as two parts across.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	And when the vein is bound, then the blood flows upwards continuously.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If the artery does not open to feeling, then you must measure the amount of space of three fingers, and cut from there down to the bone; and the quantity of blood that should be let out is six ounces, and perhaps a little more or less, depending on what the patient can endure, and the repletion of the artery; then examine the wound: if it remains over the bone with no sign of pus, then open the abscess so that it may drain, and ligate and dress the wound until it is healed.
de emigrainne	from grain
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When old grain comes, and a catarrh occurs, due to moisture from tears and heat in the temples, and ancient madness and similar things, and medicine does not help him through various methods of treatment, then we must cut the arteries in the temples and cauterize them, as we have described.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the method of extraction is for the patient to pull back the hair from his temples, and feel for the artery which opens in the temple, for it will be evident by its pulse, and is not very deep in some people who are too cold; if it is deep, the patient should stretch his neck backward with a cloth, then rub the area with some coarse cloth, and moisten the area with warm water until the artery becomes visible; then take the spatulum, from which comes the shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	then peel the skin lightly until you reach the artery, then draw it upwards with forceps and divide it well from the tissues beneath in each part; and if the artery is delicate, cut it at the tip of the fingernail, then ligate that part according to the quantity of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, then the pain will not cease at all.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And draw out blood from the vein, just to three ounces; and if the artery is large, then tie it in two places with a strong double thread of silk so that putrefaction does not come before the healing of the wound, and let the blood flow gently; then sop up the excess fluid between the two ties in that same hour, and then, if you wish, cauterize it with an iron cautery to the bone until the shoulder is cut through; and this is the main course of treatment if the patient does not have a fever and is of a hot complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For cautery helps to finish moistures; therefore it is of greater help for moistures.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	Or it is necessary for the extraction of arteries that one fills the wound with old cotton and places on it tents well made; and when they are taken off, they should be treated with dry medicines that cause charring, and with tents until it is healed; and if without cutting into the artery as far as you work, you hasten to cover by cauterization, or you employ vitriol and press it to your hand so that the blood is stanched; and if you do not have that at hand, put on the spot ice as long as the blood stops, and moisten the spot with cold water until the bleeding ceases, and then bind it as tightly as is appropriate; and what is better and easier in the extraction of an artery is to cauterize the vein with this cutting cautery of two parts, but the cutting edge should be well thickened to retain its heat longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too thin, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And you should have between the two knives a distance of a thumb's width, and then when you have burned in both places, you must put the hot iron on as far as the bone, and cut the vein in two places; and let the two heads be separated because they are not joined by this cautery all over; and this is the shape of the cautery:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When tears are flowing from the veins that are above the test of the head, and medicine does not help, and you see the face of the patient turn red, and feel pulsation in the forehead as if from trembling; and if the eyelids are drooping and moist so that the eyelashes have fallen, and the eyelids are scorched by the heat of tears, then this treatment is needed.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	And they called it in the old language "cure contused", and you should do for the patient who has this disease, cut the hairs on his forehead, then make three incisions on his forehead evenly according to the length of his forehead; let one of the incisions be as long as two fingers right through the middle of the forehead from top to bottom, and the other two at the sides above the eyes, and be careful not to cut the arteries which are at the sides above the eyes; and keep your hand away from the jaw, and let each incision be about three fingers across at a right angle to the first; and have ready a piece of sponge and a lot of cloth to wipe up the blood, then insert the spatulum all the way in where the pain is:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les .ij. fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	from the incision on the temple all the way to the second incision; and scrape all of the skin in between the two incisions down to the bone, then do the same from the middle incision to the other second one, then remove this syringe.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	then insert into the first incision the instrument called a «cultellar», which is very sharp on one side and not sharp on the other, and this is how it is shaped:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	And place the knife cutting towards the chest to the heart, and the sharp edge towards the bone, and cut as far as the middle split.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And cut all the vessels that descend from the head to the eyes until the incision is continuous to what opens in the chest, and then make another cut in the middle split to the other side; and then draw out blood equally, and press the site of the wound for the extracted blood; then insert a tent made of old cotton into each split, and apply wet rags infused with wine, oil, and garlic, and guard against hot abscesses coming; and on the third day loosen the ligature, and administer plenty of warm water, then treat the wound with basilicon ointment mixed with rose oil, and other remedies used to treat wounds, until it is healed.
dou reume des eulz	of the eyes
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	When someone has chronic cataracts, and you see their eyes are pale and small, and their vision is weakened, and the eyelids burnt, and hairs grow from them, and in their head there is sharp pain, and the patient sneezes; then know from these signs that these substances and this cataract come only from many veins, and the medicine used to treat it is like this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to look up, then make a large slit in the forehead, and another one just below it.
Et comence des la fendure de la temple senestre a la temple destre, et soit li incision jusc’a l’os; et esloigne ta main des ners des temples que muevent au mengier; et quant li os est descovers, si essue tout le sanc a une esponge, et puis desevre entre les II levres de la fendure et i met coton viel, et tentes de lin; puis lie desus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile, et te garde d’aposteme chaut; quant il est ostez, si covient que tu frottes l’os tant que chars i comence a naistre, puis le cure de choses exiccatives, que font enjanrer char.	And begin from the left temple to the right temple, and make the incision to the bone; and keep your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move the eye; and when the bone is exposed, then wipe all the blood away with a sponge, and then separate between the two lips of the slit and insert old cotton, and apply tenting with linen; then bind damp cloths soaked in wine and oil over it, and be careful about hot abscesses; once it is removed, you should rub the bone until new skin starts to form, then treat it with things that promote healing.
En teil maniere: pren .ij. parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine .iiij. parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In this way: take two parts of wheat flower, and four parts of colophony, and make an ointment from it; and administer it to the wounds to promote healing throughout.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of ear stoppers
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that falls into the ears is one of four things: grains, or insects, or minerals like iron, or similar objects. It could also be fluids like water, or garlic and similar substances.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When it falls into the ear stone or any other object that does not adhere to the ear or grow in the ear, then hold the ear towards the sun.
