Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And one uses this instrument which has .ij. tongs, of which this is the shape:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in the reason of teeth, and of this instrument which looks like large tweezers, whose shape is as follows:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this instrument be sturdy enough that it does not break, and know that many dental instruments exist; and also other instruments which are not counted; and the wise master subtlety finds his own instrument according to what his works and the disease show him, for there are many diseases for which the ancients did not teach any instrument because of their diversity. And if it does not break in the bone or in other bones, but protrudes, then he seeks the instruments that he needs, that I have told you, and helps with gestures; here is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and strong enough to hold the bone so that it does not slip, but can be held and removed; and then restore the place with appropriate medicines, and if there is a protrusion in the bone, and it is small, then treat it with this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to the natural order of the body, and its shape is unattractive, especially in virginal women, then you should know whether the tooth is new after the tooth, and is not in the right place, and cannot be filed or ground down; then pull it out; and if it is airy with the tooth, then take this instrument, of which here is the form, and is similar to a small beak, and let it be made of iron sharpened at the end:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the gum recedes a little every day because of the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it is apparent that one can be filed, then file it with a file like this is the shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is also like the file that needles are made with; and file the tooth a little every day slightly, so that it does not move until it fits; then smooth it at the end with any rasor, and if the tooth is too sharp and cuts the tongue, then file the roughness so that it is even and does not cut the tongue or corrupt speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth is loose
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth is loose from either decay or injury, and the patient cannot chew without pain, and you have tried binding medicines which did not work, then it should be restrained with a gold wire, because silver wires turn green and rust, but gold never does; and the wire should be neither too thin nor too thick, depending on the space between the teeth. If you want to extract the tooth, take the wire and wrap it around the two healthy teeth, then push the shoulder between the loose teeth until you reach the decayed tooth on the other side. Then begin covering again where you started, straining your hand gently and firmly until it is not moving; and the ligature should be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then grip the head of the tooth with tweezers and bring it together, and tie it between the healthy teeth so that it does not cut the tongue; then leave it as tightly as possible for as long as it can stay in place, and if it comes undone or the thread breaks, then tie it with another thread; it should remain in place and serve its purpose for as long as needed, and this is the shape of the teeth and the arrangement of both the healthy and the rotten ones, as you can see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when a tooth falls out, it is placed back in its place, little by little, as we have said; and no one who is not wise and experienced should meddle with this, and sometimes the shape of a tooth from a cow's bone is made, and it is put in the place where there is a defect, and it is held fast as we have said, and it remains and serves for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	to cover the line of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	Sometimes the tongue is tied underneath, either by nature as we are born, or through an accident of a wound; and the treatment is to open the mouth of the patient, and hold their head in your healthy mouth, and lift their tongue; then grip the large nerve tie with tweezers so that the tongue is loosened from its housing, and if there is swelling or a nodule due to a wound, and it has pierced the nail, then grip the nail with the tweezers and loosen the tie; and be careful not to cut too deeply into the artery underneath; once you are finished, raise the area with rosewater and garlic, or cold water, then place a tent of linen underneath the tongue; and paint the wound every night so that the edges do not fuse together.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if there is bleeding, then place vitriol on the site; and if the blood flows, then cauterize it with a lentigo cautery, which is good for this. Then treat it further until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it is black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, then do not touch it, for it is a chancre. And if it is inclining towards blenorrhea, and there is moisture, insert the nail, and open it with a subtle spatumile, and release it from one side and the other; and if the bleeding occurs while you are doing this, apply crushed vitriol until it stops, then return to your treatment until you draw out everything. Then wet the area with rose water and celery water, and treat it with other treatments until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	of abscesses in the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Sometimes there are growths in the throat called "godath", and they are properly called "almonds". When you treat them as we have described in the division, and they do not heal, be careful: if they are hard abscesses of a small size and a pale color, then do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron for fear of bleeding; but let it be until it bursts, or it will burst on its own; and if it is white and the root is thin, have a blade ready to cut it, but first examine whether the abscess is calm and soothed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore make the patient sit facing the sun, and his head be in your lap, and open his mouth and the sergeant holds his jaw between their hands, and press the tongue down to all the instrument, from which there is the shape; and it should be of silver or thin brass as well as a knife:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Having pressed the tongue down with this instrument, you will see the tonsil. Take a pair of forceps and grab the abscess, then pull it out from the tonsil, drawing any threads of membrane along with it. Then cover the instrument again to maintain its shape, for it is designed like a hook; the tip curves upward and the ends curve downward, and they are very sharp. It is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument available, you can use a pair of tweezers that are shaped like it.
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And it is sharp on one side and blunt on the other; and when you have cut one of the tonsils, then cut the other in the same way, and after the incision gargle the patient with warm water, and water and garlic, and if there is bleeding, then gargle the patient with water, or scoops of pomegranates that have been cooked, or bay leaves, and similar things, until the bleeding stops; then cure it until it is healed; and sometimes other abscesses besides the two tonsils arise in the throat, so cut them then as you did the two tonsils.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman for an abscess that was inside her throat, that is to say, the abscess was very small; and she had a swollen throat almost closed, so that the woman could not breathe through the airway, which was blocked, nor eat nor drink, and would have died if she stayed like that for another day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess had become so swollen that it had pushed up two bumps from the back of her throat.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened then, and pushed into one of the openings, then drew out a large piece of pus; then I cut into the other opening in her throat, and opened her mouth and pressed on her tongue; afterwards I pushed the probe into the abscess, and scooped out a portion of it, and only a little blood came out; and thus the airway of the woman's throat was cleared, and she began to drink water and then wine, and I continued to cut into this abscess for a long time; and it would shrink then refilled the space that I had emptied, until it became very large; afterwards, I packed it and cauterized it within her throat: thus it remained without growing; and I left these parts, and she was in God's hands after me.
de l’uve	of the liver
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the eye descends to the socket and is swollen and long, it is called "perpendicular"; if it is large and round beneath, then it is called an "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, and you see that the abscess beneath is pacified, and it is subtle; and it is rounded together and not long; and it is blood-red or a fuschia color or black, then you should avoid cutting into it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger to the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it according to the manner that I have said, from its white and length, you should cause the patient to sit facing the sun, and press his tongue against the instrument of which we spoke earlier; then pierce the eye with the needle, and draw it underneath, and scrape at it with one of the two instruments that I mentioned in the incision of the two almonds.Et s’il aduient que li cure ne profite mie, et les pustules ne se rompent mie, et la pusse n’est pas extraite, si covient que tu retires loz estrumens, et retires la pusse avec le crotin, et apaise li malaide selonc la maniere que j’ai dit ci devant.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cover anything more than the excess that is beyond the natural term; for if you cover more, it is harmful to the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we have said about the incision of the two testicles, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of covering, then you should use the cautery for the sense of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the method of the cautery is for acute ague.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the method is that the patient puts his head on your lap, and then presses his tongue against the instrument we described in the chapter on cautery, and breathes with hot air, not too thick or thin; and use the implement we described, which is shaped like this:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it has a handle at the top where the medicine is placed, like the handle of a spoon; and you place the instrument with all the medicine on the eye, and the patient lies on his side so that the saliva and mucus from the medicine do not run down into the throat and lungs; then hold your hand over the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour, until you see it harden and the burning sensation of the medicine subside. Then take some cotton, wrap it around an instrument, moisten the cotton with the medicine, and insert the instrument wrapped in cotton into the canal above, so that the cotton rests on the eye; do this frequently until the cautery is complete, then let it dry for four or five days. If you need to apply the cautery again, do so, then wash the area around the medicine with cool water, and treat the wound with gargarisms until it heals.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer than incision or cautery. If it is cured by fumigation according to this method, take calamus, hyssop, marjoram, rue, chamomile, wormwood, and similar herbs, and mix some of them in a pot with honey, and boil it; the pot should be well-glazed with strong clay, and inside the pot there is an instrument shaped like this:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be made of silver or bronze, and one end is inserted into the mouth of the patient so that the vapour rises to the eye through the canal, until the eye is mortified; then he should do this often, until the eye dries up; and take care not to do this at the beginning of a hot abscess, because many things can happen; nor should this be done beyond the decline of a hot abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, take a cane and put an egg-shell inside the end, so that the mouth of the patient is not too hot; for the egg-shell does not let the vapor burden the mouth, and it is a good treatment together with salvation.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times a fish bone or spine, or some other thing, gets stuck in the throat; so you must draw out what you can see and press the tongue against the sun with all your strength, so that you can move the object; and if it does not become apparent to you and remains stuck in the throat, you should make the patient vomit so that the food is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will come out through vomiting. Or the patient may swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a root of lettuce, or a piece of dry bread; and tie a thread to the sponge and then swallow it; and when it reaches its place, it will catch on, and then you can pull it out; and if it does not come out in the way we have said, take an instrument of lead according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And the instrument should be bent at the tip so that it can more easily enter the throat, and its tip should be lifted up; and take care not to touch the epiglottis, or it will fold over, nor push the os inside; and move it around so that the patient swallows the instrument, in order that it can dislodge the object; then he swallows it down, or you pull it out with the instrument equally, until it is out.
de la sansue de la gorge	from the mucus of the throat
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Sometimes the treatment is bleeding, as I said in the division, through the use of medicine; and when this does not help, then look at the throat of the patient towards the sun, and then press his tongue with the instrument that I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the vein, draw it out with a small hook, or with тонны thin forceps that are suitable for this.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a heated iron wrapped in a cloth, and hold it in the patient's throat; then hold the heated end of the iron to the affected area, and do this frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient has a fever all day long.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	And take a full glass of cold water and open your mouth and pour it in without swallowing and move it around with his hand often. And as soon as the patient feels the water, he should spit it out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it doesn't work as we have said, then smoke the patient with assafetida, using the instrument I described for smoking out the eye; do this several times, because it will work without bleeding.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the way to do the smoking is to take a pot with burning charcoal in it and cover it with a perforated lid, and put the instrument's head into the hole in the middle of the lid; then blow your smoke into the instrument, and the patient should put their mouth over the end of the instrument, close their mouth so that the smoke doesn't escape but goes straight to the blood; the blood will come out now, and if it doesn't, repeat the smoking many times. The patient must endure thirst and eat salty things, but not drink any water. Then it will be necessary for him to go to the toilet because of this treatment.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument used to pull out the mucus is, when you can see it, like curved tweezers that can enter the throat; and it has the shape of a bird's beak, and is coated with limestone, so that what it grabs cannot escape; and here is its shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Many kinds of abscess appear, according to what the memories that come later in this book indicate, and they differ in penetration and size; and there are two ways in which they occur, one being in their very appearance, and in what they retain moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is due to the places where they are in the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses of the head are different from those of the foundation, and the abscesses of fleshy places are different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that one must not pierce until the bowels are dead according to their fulfillment; and there are some that one must pierce when they are cruelly, and do not die according to their fulfillment, like abscesses that are near joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses occur near joints and are left until they become pus-filled around the edges, by chance the ligaments and nerves of the joint may be corrupted, causing contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or the abscess is near the principal member, and if you delay piercing it until it becomes pus-filled, it will harm the principal member; or if it is by the fundament, one should pierce it so that it may drain and not fester within, becoming elongated, and a fistula forming; nor can it heal in a short time.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And one must know the time for lancing an abscess which is mature according to its nature, and that is when the pain has subsided, and there is a reduction in fever, and lessening of pain and redness, and relaxation and softening of the head of the abscess, and other signs; and one should lance it where it is most dependant, and where there is an opening for pus to escape; and the lancing should be done from the long side of the body, and if the abscess is on the hands or feet, or in joints affecting nerves and arteries, and in all places where there is no fold.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In those who bend, according to which member.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when the abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better to let the piercing be until it becomes confirmed in completed digestion, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	Because if you pierce it in front of that, then the bowels are opened and the body is filled with filth, and perhaps the lips and the depths of him harden.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if any abscess that is pierced according to the width of the body, according to what the member needs.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must treat small abscesses with small openings; and large abscesses with large openings and many slits according to the appearance of their size; and in some abscesses where it is necessary to pierce the skin, and cover; when they have become like cloth, and are deadened, then one should do as one does with blisters: and there are some that are split into three angles; and some from which one covers as a myrtle leaf, like abscesses in the bones; and some where one makes a round incision, and other incisions and similar covers.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who have no head, such as a superficial boil, you must pierce it plainly; and when the boil is large and has drawn a great bowstring, and you pierce it, do not draw out all the bowstring in that hour, but draw out a part of it; then stop the boil until the next day, then draw out something again from it; do this several times from great to small, until the bowstring is released entirely; likewise if the patient has little strength, or is a woman carrying child, or a small child, or an elderly decrepit man.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the pus sometimes leaps out with the release of the bowstring, which might kill the patient, and you would not realize it.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore, approach this chapter with great caution, and when you have pierced the boil, wash the wound, and examine whether the wound of the boil is small; and if it is a plain cut, apply tenters made of linen or old cotton; and if it is a large boil with many openings, you should insert a tent in each opening so that they touch one another; and if you have cut into the boil in a circular manner, and washed it around, then you must fill it with old cotton or razor shavings from unbleached linen without moisture, and leave it for three days; then remove it and treat it with ointment until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if bleeding occurs in your work, bring cold water and ease, and wet the cloth, and place it over the bleeding area many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the bleeding persists, administer treatment and care, and use the powders I have described earlier in this book; and if it is winter, and the area is very nervous, then you should apply wet tents and cloths soaked in warm wine and oil; but if it is summer, and the area is fleshy, then you should apply wet cloths soaked in water and oil, or in cool wine and oil, for three days, as we have said; then loosen the abscess, wipe and treat it, as appropriate, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And now we must discuss generally about treating abscesses: I have already told you how to proceed before treating abscesses, and now see the chapter.
des soros	of sores
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	From the head come small abscesses, and they are caused by us through our clothes, just as the scabs of a chicken are, and there are many variations of them.Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some with fat and such where there is moisture as well as pus; and there are others that are hard and stony in texture, and there is no doubt if the artery does not do the opposite.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the work of the waist is that you should test all instruments called "entromissoire", from which forms come later, depending on what they contain.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, then they will release it from above.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is evacuated, then it scrapes without leaving anything behind from the skin that contains the moisture, for it returns again if you leave nothing behind; then plunge cotton in Egyptian ointment, if it is present; if not, in water and salt, and apply it to the wound, and leave it until the next day; and those who stay up all night will cure.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then restart the cotton, as before, on the second and third day, until you are sure it no longer hurts at night; then dress the wound with an ointment suitable for healing, until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess contains pus and fat, cut it according to this form, from top to bottom; and gouge out your fingers, and scrape off all of it, and put all your treatment in drawing it out through the cotton where he lies; and if the artery does not respond well, do what I have already told you.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also treat an abscess if it is a stone, and cut and dress it as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the incision on the abscess of a stone and moisture, is lighter because they are filled with less blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And some of these abscesses in the head where there is no moisture, and this was the case with an abscess I lanced on a very old woman; and I found the abscess like a hard, rough, white stone, which could not be broken; and if anyone had cut into it, it would have made them a wound as easily as a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses coming from the head, whether those that come to the heads of children or the roots of the ears, the opening should be made as low as possible in the most dependent part, so that the pus can issue; and they should be treated as appropriate.
des scrophules	of scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times abscesses occur in the neck and under the armpits, and in the groin, and sometimes elsewhere in the body, and they are large and interconnected.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly within its own part, like the ulcer and abscess of the head, as we have said; and there are many similar scrofulae.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and others that are stubborn and refuse to heal.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those where you see a healthy appearance in the touch, and it resembles the color of the rest of the body, and is not swollen on one side only, nor affecting the nerves of the neck or artery or channel, and is not deep; then you should cover it from above, and scrape away at each part, and let the two lips of the wound be at an angle, as needed, as we have said for abscesses of the head; and treat it little by little, and be careful not to cover any nerve or vein, and do not use a scalpel or knife too aggressively, so that the hand does not slip, and do not go too deep, only as much as you need.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and it does not let you work, then put crushed vitriol or some powders that stop bleeding into the wound, and bind the wound; and leave it until the abscess is quieted, and the wound is softened, and begins to fester.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the bleeding is stopped, return to your work, until you finish it; then seek with your finger if any small scrofula remains, and cut them out and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein at the root of the scrofula, you must not cut that scrofula in its root, but ligature it with a strong double thread, and let it drop without harm; then treat the wound with old cotton soaked in Egyptian ointment, and then heal it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you cut around the entire ulcer, then you must bring together the two lips of the wound and sew them up now, so that there is no superfluity remaining due to the size of the ulcer.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	you should proceed to cut off its root and pull it out, then sew it up as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those ulcers that hold superfluity, pierce where it appears to be dying; and pierce it thus as the one before was described, depending on it, then apply bandages with ointment and similar things so that it corrupts what remains of the corruption; and when the wound is clean, then cure it with ointment smeared on a cloth until it is healed.
de squinance	of squint.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancients wrote and spoke of throat-slitting; but I have never seen it done in our land, and this is the script of their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with squint, it is necessary that the flap of the throat, which is called the "epiglottis", be cut; and one should not make an incision through this, because all the veins and the lung of the patient are in those who have a hot abscess in the mouth, or in the throat, or in both armpits.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the lung, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent loss of life due to strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to split the epiglottis, we should split it below three circles or four, a small split across, between the two circles or according to the amount of the split in the soft palate; and those parts which are subject to the splitting of the epiglottis so that there is no flesh, and the vessels are long from it.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is fearful, he should stretch the skin of the throat all the way to the Adam's apple, then split the larynx until it reaches the voice box; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see any, and then close the wound, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the artery of the voice box which leaps out through the broken place, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open a little.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed in which one fears strangulation, bring together the two lips of the wound in the neck, and stitch it up all the way to the cartilage without leaving a gap; then administer remedies that promote healing until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says that one should not do this until the throat is completely swollen and the patient is judged to be at death's door and the shortage of breath.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then close the epiglottis so that the patient cannot choke, and he will breathe through the wound, and thus is kept from dying; and because of this, the ancients commanded to leave the wound open until the mischief of the disease had passed, and it passes in 3 or 4 days. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and cure it, once it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a young girl take a knife and stick it in her throat, and cut part of the windpipe; I was called to heal her, and found her as good as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound and found that the blood which had issued from it had not flowed out any further than the throat, and the blood vessels were intact.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hurried and sewed up the wound, and healed her until she was cured; and the young girl had only hoarseness afterwards, and returned to her natural state; therefore I say that one should not be afraid to cut into the epiglottis.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	This abscess is called a "throat hernia", and it is a large abscess the color of a plum, and it occurs often in women; and there are two kinds: natural and accidental; a natural one has no cause.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental kind is in two ways: one is like a cyst, and the other way is like an abscess that comes from an artery; there is doubt about it, and one should not use strong remedies except on one that is small, and test and examine throughout the whole entrance: if you find it just like a cyst, and it cannot go anywhere, cut it open as one cuts a cyst, and treat it all over its surface, if there is nothing inside; then examine carefully and heal it as it should be.
des nous	from us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways of doing this, all of which I will describe; but now I must explain the difference between a cut and an incision.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that a discharge is a persistent fever and heat until the boil has burst and completed its course; then the fever and heat will cease.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With a cut there is no heat or fever or pain; it contains pus, which is its own sac and follows the color of the body; it begins like a pustule and becomes large; there are two appearances, either dry or moist, and in terms of color they are as I have described in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the treatment of a boil, you must first test and examine it with an instrument called a "probes", according to what its shape indicates in the chapter that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the way to inquire into abscesses is to squeeze the most moist part that you find in the abscess, and keep squeezing gently until you feel that the pus has broken through the skin, then it should be according to the size of the abscess; then extract the instrument, and take care not to squeeze anything out.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the pus is flowing freely, whatever color it has, treat it as I have described for other abscesses; and if after squeezing with the instrument no pus comes out, know that it is solid, so do this in a cross shape, and take hold of it with tweezers, and gently scrape off the skin on each side and guard the wound so that you draw it out cleanly with the cut; and if you cannot draw it out cleanly, then draw it out in pieces so that nothing remains.Et se li moistor ne veult pas correre de la croiz, si le fent en rond et non pas en croiz, car il n’est selonc la croiz que li moistors veulten corer; et si aprés ce que tu as tiriet la cotte, s’il demoure encores quelque chose dedenz l’aposteme, si le traies a la fine par pieces tant qu’il soit tout traiez.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	Because if it is not removed, then the nail will return many times; and if a little of it remains and does not hurt you, then employ some corrosive powder on the wound, and constrict the wound, and put warm poultices on it, and treat it with other remedies until it is healed; and if the nail is large, then cut its two lips, and treat it with that which softens meat.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	and if the vein is pulsating, or any other vein that you are hastening, use vitriol and leave it for 2 or 3 days until the wound suppurates and the bleeding stops; then return to the cupping as before.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of the trocar, which come in three varieties: large, medium, and small; and there are three types of these, called 'albaret', and one called 'breb'; and they also come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the aperture of the fistula; and they are similar to the needles used to pierce sorcerers' marks, and are made of brass, iron, or silver, but the yellow ones are best, and have been proven with black pitch to pierce fistulas; and they come in three sizes: large, medium, and small, according to the size of the aperture.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of warts are very diverse, as you can see: large, medium, and small; and there are warts that have two curves in three ways as well; and there are warts that have three curves and are also in three ways; and there are warts that have two curves and only one curve, and they are in three ways; and all of these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The heads of these instruments are sharp, and some only cut from one side, so that they do not cut the vein or nerve; and there are small tools that are used in wounds, so that the patient does not suffer when opening abscesses; and they are of three types: large, small, and medium, as you can see; and they are only used on fleshy parts, such as legs, arms, breasts, and similar areas; and sometimes another small instrument is made, resembling a slice of a finger, according to this shape, with which blood is stopped.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and it is sometimes put in the place that heals by copious bleeding of the veins and arteries, and sometimes they are made according to this large form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	At times, the breasts of some men become swollen when they are infected, and they look like women's breasts; they remain disfigured and swollen. If one wants to cure them, he should follow this recipe from line b to g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Scrape off the fat, and treat the wound with ointment containing cauterizing ingredients, then stitch together the two lips of the wound, and heal it until it is clean; and if the breast hangs down, and has become soft because of its size as it does in women, then make two incisions on top, at each side, so that one cut holds the other at their ends, with the longest cut containing the shortest according to this illustration, from line b. to g.; then scrape off the skin between the two lips, remove the fat, and apply what we have described regarding stitching and powders, and anything else necessary for healing, until it is healed; and if it is not healed, or the incision is not entirely made, because the patient does not want to rest, or due to bleeding, then you should fill the wound with wet cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until it dissolves the remaining fat and the skin, then heal it until it is clean.
des apostemes des asselles	of abscesses of the armpit
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These abscesses that come from under the armpit are like hard scrofula nodules, some of which contain pus and moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Those who contain moisture should be cut according to this form, from line .b. up to line .g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the pus that is in the abscess has been discharged, then fill the wound with clean cotton, and leave it until the next day; then remove all the cotton and treat it with an appropriate ointment until it is healed.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscesses are similar to scrofula, they should be treated as we have said for fissures of scrofula, and if the wound is deep, then apply cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of bleeding from an artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is swollen and the skin above it, then abscesses often form, and also swelling of the vein; and so one knows that it is caused by the artery when the abscesses are long and deep; and when you touch them with your fingers, you feel a pulling; and when it is caused by the vein, there is a deflating pus coming out; and it is foolish to cover this abscess, especially when it is below the armpit or under the jaw and neck or in many other places, and it is large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore one must avoid using an iron cautery, and if there is one on the head, then that one also; and when there is swelling from an artery above the skin, make a cut along the length of the artery from line .b. to line .g.; then open the skin at the edges, and carefully separate the artery from the flesh, so that it is exposed; then insert a needle underneath the artery, and pierce it through to the other side, and constrict the artery with a double thread in two places, according to what I taught you in the extraction of the two temporal arteries; then pierce the area between the two threads with an introducer, so that the blood inside flows out, and so release the abscess; then administer the cure by squeezing bowels, until the ligature slips off; then treat it with the appropriate ointment, until it is healed; and if the abscess is caused by the vein, then one must dye their hand with the pus from the abscess to the skin, then insert a needle underneath the area where they are holding the hand, and pierce it, and insert a double thread, so that you draw it through to the other side; then tie off the abscess, as I told you, at the ligature in either one of the two places; and if you doubt that the threads will slip out, then insert another needle underneath the entire abscess at the incision of the first needle, and pierce through, and constrict the threads in four places; then cover the abscess so that the superfluity flows out, then cover the superfluity with a moistened cloth in wine and oil, then administer treatments of tenting and ointments until it is healed.
des apostemes des ners	of abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	As well as abscesses coming in the artery and vein, they come to the nerves when they are injured, or from too much work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this happens most often in the shoulders and elbows and everywhere where there are joints, and it is a deep abscess, and its color resembles the color of the body, and it is in various states without pain; and when one applies pressure to it properly, the patient feels pain, and it is not throughout the body but under the heart; and it is mute from all sides, and does not go forward or backward, or down or up, and that which is in joints should not be covered by iron: otherwise there will be contraction; and that which is on the head or forehead, treat with a poultice.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, hold it with tweezers and pull out the root; if it is large, cut into it with a knife, and scrape away the flesh, then cut out the bone and sew up the wound, and heal it until it is cured.
des grosses boces pendans	large boils hanging
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	At times it happens in the belly and nowhere else; it is a disease called "mushroom" due to its resemblance to mushrooms, with thin roots and thick stems. There are small ones and very large ones. I once saw a man who had two in his belly that looked more like mushrooms than anything else, with no difference between them, white in color, with fine roots, and split open, from which moisture would flow.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I cut them open and found one weighing 18 ounces and the other 6 ounces, and their appearance in the incision is such that you should check if the disease is moist, and the color of the joint is white and moist with thin roots; then cut it with a spatulum, and have the fire cautery ready in your presence.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Because excessive bleeding often occurs when cutting, and if the blood flows, then hasten to cauterize it; and if you see the disease is frightened and fearful of the iron incision, take a well-prepared thread and tie the joint as we have said, and leave it for two days; then constrict it, and do not stop squeezing the thread until he cuts the joint, and it comes out without any effort; and if the roots are thick, then cut with fear for the belly, but you can certainly cut half of it, then cauterize it so that it does not return; then treat the wound, and be careful not to cut the belly which is of a purplish color and of poor sense and milky appearance.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an encrusted abscess, and I will come to the treatment of cancer later.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the boil pops
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the appearance of the boil comes from cauterization of a wound or from a fissure in a syphilitic sore, and it is on the abdomen and some of the bowels, as happens with other ulcers, or from blood that flows from veins or arteries according to what is in front, or from wind; and if it is through the ulceration of the syphilitic sore and through the outlet of the bowel, then the color of the abscess is similar to the color of the body, and it is a light thing without pain, and there are various outlets.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is from the exit of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it with their fingers, it rises, and then returns, and sometimes it is serous, and increases a lot at the entrance of the bath and with great effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and it opens up well when you press it with your hand, and it does not constrict; and if it is due to blood, then the abscesses are large and hard, and they are fixed according to a quantity; and if it is due to wind, then it is soft on touch, and the work is that you look to see if the appearance is due to blood from an artery or vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you need to let the wound heal.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I told you in the chapter on abscesses, about the artery and the vein.
