And the treatment of men and women is that you bandage all the joints tightly, and treat them like other wounds; in the second method, for men whose urine leaks through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tetter
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	A tent is a swollen joint on the natural part, so that it is too ugly to look at; and some women have them as large as a hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	You should dye the excess of the tent with your hand or a cloth, and bind it gently; and do not go too deep, lest bleeding comes from it, then cure another cure until it is healed; and to another wound that occurs at the mouth of the navel, use cow's dung, and perhaps it will work, and it is like the appearance of a cow, and because of this they called it the "cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you must cut it, as we have said above, treat and cure it until it heals.
de erratique	of erratics
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	It is errant when the nature of the woman is not perceived, or the passage is small; and it is natural at birth, or accidental due to illness that comes to her; or it is due to a foreign object, or a thin or thick cyst, and it is formed deep in the pelvis, or on the sides, or below, or wherever; and they should understand conception and childbirth, and possibly flowers to have; and the knowledge of these things is through observing the dance.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the tumors are nearby and apparent, then use your fingers or a stick.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is from a thin cyst and it is nearby the lips, then do this: place your two index fingers together, and let the woman lie on her back with her legs spread; then form the lips so that the thin cyst is pierced and cover the tumor; then take wool, moisten it in oil, and place it over the area, and let the woman rest at home every day so that it does not close up.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the ulcer is hard and dense, then you must cup it with spatule resembling a myrtle leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the swelling is from fresh flesh, soak it with vinegar and cup it; and have medicines to stop bleeding, such as ake, dragon's blood, incense, and yolk of egg; then apply a broad piece of wool so that the wound does not close; and thus for a long time, and apply a tent of dry linen; then treat with other treatments until it is healed.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when in the wound there is fresh flesh, it must be cupped in this way, unless it is an abscess.Et s’il y a en l’un d’eiles ou d’autes membres de l’artere, si que li sang soit distenduz, si covient qu’on le tienne ben estainchiez et la coute a la raie; et s’il y a aposteme enchancre, si covient qu’il le fasse inciser sus la veine.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For an abscess in the head, one must not touch it with fire.
des emorroides	of hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Hemorrhoids are opened veins from which blood flows, and when hemorrhoids are old, they become الثؤلول; and we have already discussed their appearances and signs in the previous division, and I will now describe those that are curable.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and الثؤلول, when they are emp- by fire in the head, and do not appear to be felt, are not cured by iron.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those that are at the mouth of the head, one can feel, are those that can be cured.Si li emorroide est en la marris et n’est mie emp-, si covient le fer curer.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is necessary, then, to place the woman in a cool house, and then heat the bed with tongs, and the comforter at its roots, and then powder over blood-restraining medicines, such as acacia and dragon's blood and incense, and similar things; then, bind her feet to the wall for an hour, then place her in cold water; and if there is bleeding, have her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate peel and gallnuts and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and garlic, and make a plaster with it on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	If not, have her breathe in steam from the back and breasts without burning; then take wool, and soak it in plantain juice or in dogwood juice mixed with old wine, and apply it to the area.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has settled, then treat the area with ointment until it is healed; and that which is called "albathir" is red and resembles coarse wool, so it should be covered as I said before; and then treat it until it is healed.
des apostemes de la marris	Here is the translation of the provided text:
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	There are many types of abscess that come about in the body, such as cancers and piercings, and herpes, and boils, and wounds, and hemorrhoids, and hot abscesses, and various other ailments which I have discussed in the classification.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	Therefore, I will discuss in this treatise the hot abscess that occurs in the body, which is not among those that discharge pus; and if you want to know about iron treatment, then observe whether the abscess is painful at the onset of its appearance, and filled with heat and fever, and whether it turns red if you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore, do not hurry to pierce it, but let the pain subside; then have the patient sit on a chair, with two small seats to lean against, and support his back, and bring his feet together to one side of his leg; let his thighs be spread apart, and place his arms under his knees, and tie them well with a bandage; then suck the wound towards the right side, and administer the instrument used to open the mouth of the wound, from which the abscess will form; you must insert the rod first to determine the depth of the wound, so that what enters the wound does not go deeper than it should, and does not hurt the patient; if the instrument is larger, cover the wound with cloth so that it does not cause discomfort; the patient should hold the spout of the instrument, and you should heat the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is opened and they do it on the soft hand, then it should be covered with a poultice of the chief or with a spatumile. And when the bowel is evacuated, then you should put into the wound wet tents in rose oil, or in dry green oil; and put the tent outside the wound at the bottom of the injury, and put a bandage over the injury and over the clean, moist lamb's wool in water or malva leaves that have been cooked; then cure after two days of ointment, until it is healed. And sometimes raise the injury and the wound by a clyster of water and honey, and then with water or roots of iris and aristology that are cooked for a long time; then return to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is retracted into the injury, you should not cook with iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth

Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if it is administered to patients with abscesses that occur in the sea; and if bleeding occurs, it should be immersed in restraining water, and other remedies should be administered.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman who had had a dead fetus in her womb, then another was sewn over it, and the other died.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, she got an abscess in her armpit, which swelled up so much that it opened and began to discharge greatly.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to the cure, and I thought long and hard, but could not heal the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I applied a strong吸引 plaster, and out came a bone, and after a few days, some more.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very wonderstruck, for I see that the belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that these were the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I wanted to see the wound and hands of os, so that the woman was in a better place; and the woman lived a long time like this, and then became a little bow-legged; and I did not remember this chapter except that when the master finds something strange, he knows how to put it right.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the bone back to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Hereafter comes the form of the press, with which one is weaned; and at .ij. turnings at .ij. heads of .ij. strings.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more subtle than the restrictor, and they should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the fust should be two fingers wide, and the edges of the trees should be one palm long or a little more; and in between the two limbs there should be two adjustments of this same wood, which are firmly attached to one another, half a palm or a little more in length; and these two adjustments are inserted into the mouth of the sea to open when you turn the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, with its appearance more subtle and lighter, is made of ebony wood or boxwood, according to the likeness of tongs; and has at each end two adjustments, as you see, a palm-width long, and two fingers wide; and when you see to open the instrument throughout, then let the woman lie on her back, her feet dangling and her legs open, then fit together the two adjustments in the instrument, and hold the head of the instrument underneath between her thighs; then work your hand throughout the instrument, as you have done with tongs equally, according to the quantity that you see opening the mouth of the instrument, until the midwife does what she wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all decorated and have many similarities; and when the surgeon prepares them, the work is faster and easier for the patient due to their design.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	Do not be discouraged by the instrument until you have prepared it, for their necessity is inexcusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the afterbirth is retained in childbirth, then you must instruct the patient to hold her breath, and then make her sneeze with some scent, and pinch her hands to her mouth and nose; and if she passes gas through these means, all the better.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If not, they take a pot and make an opening in the lid, and put in herbs that can open the mouth of the wound, such as camomile, rue, anise, cassia, and centaury; all these herbs, or some of them, are cooked in water over fire; then they put one end of the pot into the opening, and the other end into the mouth of the wound, and they apply it so that the vapors enter the wound; then they make the patient sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	Then let the secondine boil gently.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	And if it remains after this treatment and does not go away, instruct the midwife to moisten her left hand in oil of sesamum or in mussel-shell oil, and then put it into her natural passage, and search for the placenta; and when she has found it, she should grasp it and gently stretch it, so that the wound is not torn during extraction; but she must move it slightly to the right and left, and then pull; then it will come out.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the opening of the wound is narrow, we have discussed the treatment of sneezing and fumigation with herbs; and if it is not healed by all that we have said, then be sure not to foolishly use a cauterization; but it is fitting that what is at the mouth of the wound, you should tie it to the thigh of the woman, then cleanse it with an ointment of tetrafarmaçon; then she will pass wind and recover, and the odor will come out; but nonetheless, when she passes wind, a bad odor comes to the stomach and head, and the illness worsens.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	So, therefore, suitable fumigations are necessary: some of the ancients have tried fumigation with watercress and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The shape of the instrument with which one smokes out the woman in retention of flowers and secundines, if it is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	It is like glass in appearance, and its head is sharp in nature, and its shoulders are wide above the fire; and the fumigation is over charcoal, and the teign until it is wasted, and another begins anew.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who do not have the anus pierced, but the rectum is closed with a thin membrane; therefore, it is necessary for the midwife to pierce that membrane with her finger, and not pierce it with a spitful, and keep the bandage so that it does not touch it; then put on wet linen in wine and oil, then treat with ointment until it heals.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will heal, put a wooden rod in the wound and leave it for several days, then remove it when the child wants to walk around.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And sometimes this clotting comes suddenly from a wound or an abscess; then it must be covered suddenly: then it should be treated, as we have said, with a rod of pine.
de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula in the fundament
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from under the anus are nodular and grow larger than those that come from within the anus, or in the space between the two parts, whether there is one fistula or several; and when this nodulation is old, it opens and discharges moisture, or a white or thin pus, and sometimes these fistulas are ulcerated. They are perceived by what comes out of them, either through urination or flatulence, when the patient expels gas, and sometimes they discharge pus.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And there are fistulas that pierce all the way to the bladder, and halfway down the penis; and they reach the hip joint and up to the testicles.The following text is a medieval medical treatise written in Old French, around the 12th-13th centuries.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And so one recognizes a fistula that is ulcerated at the anus, and not one that is not: and it is when you put your index finger into the anus, and insert a thin needle of brass or iron into the fistula when there is no bending or crook to it.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is a crook to it, one inserts a thin tent of lead or horsehair into the fistula as far as one can feel the tent or hair with their finger; and if one cannot feel it, and no pus, flatulence, or wind comes out of the fistula, as we have said, then know that it does not pierce through; so hasten to cure it.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula has reached the bladder or urinary tract, and the urine leaks out, and cannot be stopped by medicine.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perceived just to the joint of the thigh, then the vein flows just to the site; if there is no tortuosity and the pain is felt all around, then it goes right into the bowels, and neither medicine nor ointment helps; and in these persisting fistulas, there is no cure other than labor and the vanity of foolish glances that interfere.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In one that is not perspiring and is not old, there is hope of healing by iron, as I have experienced; and the patient lies on his back, and lifts his legs up to his thighs, and has his thighs tilted towards his belly; then insert an iron tent, or a lead one if there is tortuosity, as far as you can tell where the vein flows.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels it around the anus, then you must insert your index finger, provided that you feel that the vein has pierced through; and if it is uncovered where you feel between your finger and the flesh, then you know that it is perspiring; do not work on it any further, for one cannot heal it.Si li tenture est alons et ne torce mie, si a grant esperance de saniteit; s’il torce et est tortuosite, si n’a point de saniteit, si com j’ai esproveit.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	One can indeed heal some of these, but this happens rarely; and the help that one gives is to heat the cautery sutilly according to the width of the fistula, as it is said before; and one fills it entirely hot in the fistula, until it comes out from under the anus; and one does this twice or three times, until one knows that these false flesh are burned, which look like a bird's feather; and then one cleans with moist bandages, until this flesh comes off, and then one treats with ointment, binding up and healing.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is thus healed, that is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it cannot be healed otherwise; and if the tent enters and does not pierce to the anus which is at the fundament, and there is between your finger and the tent a thick covering of false flesh or syphilis, and you see the fistula above this covering toward the anus; then cut off the beginning of the fistula, and fill it up in front of the tent, and then cauterize after, until it reaches the tip of the tent; and the tent will be released and fall out; then clean away that false flesh which looks like a bird's feather, and nothing will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the pus flows, and cuts between you and the wound, then cauterize it with fire or with medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery draws together two things: namely, the burning of the flesh around the wound and the stanching of blood and the drying up of moisture; then treat the tent with butter or crushed substance until the bowels gush out, and let the burnt flesh come out in the bowels; then treat the wound with soothing ointments on hard charcoal, and the medicines are dry.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, it is healed and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes all the way from the fundament, and is distant from the body, put your finger in the fundament, and probe it.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent and between two is the membrane or flesh, or it is about to pierce through, do not lose heart and hope by using one of three methods: either cauterize as we have said, or cut to the bottom, or if you can, insert a tent and treat as first; but do not go too deep so that you do not disturb the lining which holds the foundation, and let the evacuations occur through there willingly; then treat as we have said; perhaps it will be healed. Or remove this covering and cleanse after it has been cut away from under the foundation, either by tent or other pointed instrument; then clean the wounded flesh that is in the wound, as much as you can; then try to restore the wound and keep the fistula in the part away from the foundation: then it will be a lighter burden on the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And sometimes there are fistulas in this way: and it is when you put the tent into the fistula, and it is on the side of the foundation next to the skin above, then take a tent pierced at the top according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And he inserts a twisted thread into the tent, and inserts the tent into the fistula all the way to the tip.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is punctured at the margin of the foundation inside, then pull out the thread from that opening, so that you push your finger into the foundation; and draw the end of the thread, and bring the two heads together, and press them against each other, and leave it for one or two days; and sometimes they are constricted, as long as the threads cut through the membranes between them, and close up; then cure the wound until it is sewn and healed.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not drain, then have it drained in every way you can, if it is not too deep.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not advisable to bandage it so tightly during the bleeding, and then during the treatment, as we have said, until he is healed.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The shape of the thorny spatumile which one uses to make a fistula is very sharp on one side and smooth on the other; and on the sharp side it does not cut what it should not, as you see here:
des emorroydes	of hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two types: they can be inside the anus, like grains of resin, with both small and large ones, and some draw blood, and there can be one or more of them, and they can be outside the anus and at the top of the anus; but those that are outside have little moisture, and yet they often draw a little yellow water or blood, and they are colored like the rest of the body. The treatment for those who have them inside is to make the patient strain while defecating so that the hemorrhoids come out, and when the veins appear, you hurry and grab them with tweezers or your fingernail, then pinch them at their roots; if the nails cannot hold them due to moisture, they are grabbed with a piece of cloth or cotton or a piece of camel's hair, then pulled out with the fingers, pinched, and powdered with some hot powder that is used for cauterization; or they can be cauterized as described in the chapter on cauterization, and then other treatments can be applied until they heal. If the anus cannot come out, then the patient should be given a strong and sharp enema to clean what is inside the anus so that it can come out clearly; when the hemorrhoids come out and the veins have left the anus, the treatment is easy; you grab them with your fingernail or tweezers, pinch them, then treat them as we have said until they heal and fear incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you wish to perform the suturing in this manner: take a twisted thread and insert it into a needle; then pull the thread through from the top, and pierce the needle from the other side; turn both ends of the thread under the needle, and leave it slack; tighten the thread firmly, then tie it off, and remove the needle; do likewise with all the others, leaving one to draw out any excess blood; next, place a damp cloth soaked in rose oil or cerate over the wound, and command the patient to rest; then let him remain until he has defecated, and once he has done so, treat the wound with ointment and other remedies until it is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	from dryness of the anus or rectum
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Drying of the bowels occurs often in the intestines, due to constipation or when the illness is old and medicine doesn't help.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you wish to use a spatulum or your fingernail to scrape away the superficial scabs without allowing them to become moist; then treat the wound until it is firm and healed; if it cannot heal, then repeat the scraping more vigorously than before, until it is fully healed and scrapes away.
dou fremit	where there is trembling
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Ant is a small creature that moves about the body, and sometimes it bites, and one feels it like a shiver, and it goes throughout the body, and more in the hands than elsewhere.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And its cure is to take a straw of goose feather, or a strong vulture feather, and place that straw on the shiver, until the purple circle has surrounded the shiver; then turn your hand along the entire straw, until you cup all around the shiver, and pull it deeply, and pull out the shiver by its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, make this out of a feather of bronze or iron according to this shape, and let it be thin underneath and curved on top.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	do not pierce it, so that it can hold the vein, and squeeze it And if you see, cauterize the vein, as it is before in the chapter on cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the enema
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Sometimes an enema is made of silver or brass, or of melted copper or small and large stones, depending on the person to whom they are administered.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those which are administered to children and those who are weak and in pain are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and large enema is above wide, or the stomach is bound according to this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And it has a bulge where the belly is tied, as you see, and the buttocks are pierced inside; and it has two openings on one side, and one on the other; and the belly is where one puts the medicine in a beast's bladder or parchment, and it is pierced all around with small holes, and there is an inch of space between each hole, then tie into these holes a strong thread of twisted thread in an X or spiral around, and gather the belly as if it were a goat; and when the medicine is inside, then tie it to the instrument in front with a strong thread, and then catheterize; and this is the shape of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	Let the medicine be neither too hot nor too cold, and anoint the head with oil or egg white, or similar, then insert it gently; then the minister should squeeze it with both hands together until it is all released, then remove the enema, and let the patient lie on his side, and if the medicine wants to come out, let him hold it as long as he can; and if he sleeps for a night afterwards, it will be of greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you catheterize him for a flux of the belly, and the medicine rushes out, then he should repeat it until he is cured.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are in the anus or rectum, then let the enema be as fine as for a child; and this is how to make the fine enema that the skin is stretched:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already discussed in the division about the treatment of wounds; now we will discuss the treatments by hand and medicine, according to the completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to how they are made, and according to the places where the wounds are made, and according to what makes them.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are through the impact of stone, and cutting with sword and knife, or lance or club or arrow, or similar objects; or they are made according to the places in the body, such as a wound that falls on the neck, or head, or foot, or belly, or liver, and similar members; and I will tell you the cure for each wound, and begin with the wounds of the head which are simple, for the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes to the head, and the bone is not broken, one should take care if it is from a stone or similar object, and the skin is still broken and the wound is large, and you quickly doubt a hot abscess: then let him immediately bloodlet with the cephalic itself if there is little blood coming from the wound, and the bleeding should be in the opposite direction of the injured part; and let the patient avoid repletion of wine and rich foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if he does not want to bloodlet, then let his food be diminished, and do not drink wine or eat meat; and put on the wound, if hot abscesses come out, cotton wet only in rose oil, or in astringent wine; and if there is no hot abscess, then put on the wound, if it has all its blood and is not moved by air, powder which I will describe a little later; and if it was moved by fire, then put on some ointments until it is healed.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large like that of a sword and similar, and the lips cannot be brought together with stitches, then bring them together with sutures, as I will describe for abdominal wounds.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and there is no more than a small piece of flesh holding it together, then cut it; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore hard flesh in place of skin, and instruct the patient to eat coarse meats, such as testes and cooked wheat, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find pustules on the skin, and it is not attached to the bone, then cut off the pustule, and let the pus flow out; then cure it. And if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which will not stop bleeding, and medicine does not help, then tie a string around it; and if that does not work, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, the cure is easy: you must apply this powder which will heal as soon as the burn has healed.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method of the powder is as follows: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; quicklime three parts, and powdered very finely, and apply it to the wound, and bind it tightly, so that it heals well and joins all its blood; and then bandage it well, and leave it loose if it swells; for the medicine is not removed until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And sometimes one should use chalks only when one doesn't have incense or dragon's blood, but only when the wound has healed.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the burn has moved the wound, and is in the same place, do not apply any of this powder to it; but apply some soothing ointments, or a poultice made from barley flour mixed with water and honey, until it turns yellow; then cure it with other cures until it heals.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	If the fracture of the bone comes with the wound, and it is small, I will extract it with tiny pincers; and I will tell you about fractures of the head later.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound in the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is on the neck and it is single, there is no difference between it and that of the head, except that the nerves or artery of the neck may be cut.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is a nerve, there is nothing else to do but let the cure proceed, and not apply anything constricting, for it harms the nerves and makes them retract; and do not put anything cold on the wound, for the substance of the nerves is cold, and their continuation with the brain, which is the highest member; but use medicated wines, such as washed wine in warm water, and mixed with rose oil, and cooked wine also in warm water, and other minerals according to this method, and moist ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, cut and ligature it with bandages, then treat it until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and it is chapped and full of pus, then pierce it or cut lower down; and if the artery is cut and bleeding ensues, stop it, and ligature it, and cauterize if necessary; and if the spine of the throat is cut, or the carotid, and the conduit is blocked through which food passes, then cut along the keel on the throat, and do not touch the throat but reset it according to its natural shape; and then ligature it appropriately, and leave it for several days, then clean with a poultice until it heals; and if the wound has left an impression in the bone, then drill it out; and if there are pieces of bone, then extract them all if you can, and those that you cannot reach, leave them until the wound heals, and the opening is closed and ligatured. And if the wound is fresh, then powder with the powder I have described.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is a fistula, treat it as I have described in its chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound of spear or knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a stab wound from a lance or knife, and the wound is deep, then examine if the wound bleeds until the patient faints: then you know that the wound is deadly; and if it is not deep, and the wound is fresh with all its blood, then do not put the powder on in the first hour, or tie it for the blood to drain out completely, and return to the heart, and kill the patient; but apply an attractive ointment, and bind it twice a day; and if you don't have an ointment, then place old cotton in the wound to absorb moisture, and let the patient sleep on the wound for three, or four, or more days; then no spasms, nor tremors of the heart, nor strangenesses of the soul will come; and when you see good signs, then you know that the wound is healed.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat it therefore with poultices and other remedies until it heals; and if it cannot heal, and the wound remains open, then you know there is a fistula; treat it as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a cut by sword or knife, and it is simple, on the chest or back, then treat it as one who is in front; if it is large, stitch it; and if it is small, apply powder to it, and if it is pressed into the bone, and has chipped pieces, then cleanse the wound, and draw out the foreign objects if they are loose; and if they are not loose, let the wound fester, so as to lessen the extraction; and for other wounds in other limbs, judge as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	from a rupture in the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	There are great, medium and small ruptures of the belly; from the large wound sometimes the intestine, or the nerve of the intestines, comes out through which there is an entrance for air; and stitching is more difficult, and sometimes the smaller wound is worse than the larger one, because one must stitch the intestines in more carefully by degrees; because the intestines swell as soon as they feel cold, so they go back in more easily, and therefore it is better to heal the smaller wound, so that one can reset the intestine to its place before the others. And know that there are four types of rupture of the belly: the two common stitches occur in the belly stitch, and the stitch of other wounds on the body; and II other own stitches are common to other wounds; and nevertheless they are more appropriate with the belly stitch, and I will say one by one and explain.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and some part of the intestines has protruded, and the diseased part must be removed by one of two ways: either because of the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen due to cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm it in such a way: moisten a sponge or soft cloth in lukewarm water, or boil it in squinting water and cypress and spice, and rose the intestines until the swelling is removed; and sometimes this wine-based restringent is made, and it is only applied to reduce the swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling go down, wet the intestines with water or warm and mild wine, for through this the entrance is narrowed by a little; and if it cannot enter, then they make a small incision in the wound using an instrument, as one does to treat hemorrhoids; and the first remedy is better than cutting, which no one should do without great necessity; and the instrument for splitting it is: insert it into the bend and push out, and see the shape here:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged and the intestines burst out, then put them back in according to their natural form in their proper place, if you have the power, because this is worth it.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is lower in the abdomen, you should make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs above his head, and if it is higher up in the abdomen, then he should lie on his side with his head and feet higher than the lower parts, and also if the rupture is in one of the two sides, then the wounded part must be higher than the other. And thus you should arrange what I say for great and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, use what you have at hand, and then take a needle or more, according to the quantity of the wound's size, and leave a space between the head of the wound, and insert a needle where there is a good strong thread; and pierce both sides of the skin with two sides of the sinew, which is under the skin inside, so that you make it pierce from that part, and assemble the two heads of the sinew together; then tie the thread around the needle twice on each side, then assemble the two sides of the wound properly, and then leave a space, and insert another needle, then tie the thread as you did with the first needle, and don't stop doing this according to how many needles you need, until the entire wound is bound; the needles should be medium-sized between thin and thick, because thin needles cut through the flesh, and the too thick ones cannot enter well: so they should be medium-sized. And do not push the needles too deep into the flesh and skin, so that they cut and open the wound before it heals; then tie the ends of the needles, so that they don't hurt the patient when he sleeps, and put tents or rags on the ends of the needles to hold them in place, and leave them until the wound is healed. This method of sewing with needles is most suitable for small wounds, as there is enough room for one needle or two. The second type of sewing is common, and it is that you assemble the two sides of the skin and the two sides of the sinew together on a needle with a strong medium thread; and when you have pierced these four sides, bring the needle back to the part where you started, in the manner that one sews a cloth; and leave a space between each stitch the thickness of a finger's width. This sewing is suitable for a man, and I sewed a wound on a man's abdomen, which had been cut with a knife, and the wound was more than a palm wide, and the intestines were protruding more than two palms, and the wound was in the middle of the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I returned to him the intestine after it had been outside for 24 hours, and the wound was sewn shut for 15 days, and I healed it, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And they had pronounced sentence on him that he would die, and it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, for I was in a place where there was no medicine or ointments to be found; and I put clean cotton over the wound twice a day, and washed it with water and honey until he recovered.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Now I will tell you about two proper methods of sewing: take the needle and pierce it through the edge of the wound from the outside in until it touches the skin; then, while still piercing from the outside in, bring the needle out the other side of the wound and into the skin again; the idea behind this sewing method is to do it like a tailor sews pelts, going back and forth between the two sides of the wound until the whole seam is complete.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of suturing, which Galen describes properly, is like that used by some who join two pieces of skin together naturally, and apply one end of the stitch to the other, in such a way: pierce an needle into the proximity of the edge, and only pierce that spot, leaving the two ends of the wound; then turn the needle and pierce from the outside inwards, all the way through to the inside, through the two ends of the wound; then pierce one and then the other from the outside inwards, through two other points on the skin near the edge on the opposite side; this is the most common and best method of suturing.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen says this, and some testify to it: one should sew the abdomen with two needles, with thread in each; and one should push one needle from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew wounds; and know that when the stitch is on the abdomen, it is more painful than in other places on the abdomen.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are like the judgments of other wounds: and it is that when you find the fresh wound full of blood, as soon as the burn has moved, so that the intestine returns and the gut; then put on the powder of the charm, and if the burn has moved, put on any ointment that is present, until the wound heals; and tie the threads, and sew up the lips and the mirach; then cure the wound like the others, until it is healed; and if you do not have medicine, as soon as it begins to heal, put old cotton on it and move it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need any other medicine in many cases where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will cause infection in the principal members, you should moisten a light linen cloth with tempered oil, or rose oil, and put it around the angles, and under the armpits; and if there is pain or pus in the bowels, which often happens, then cleanse them with warm black wine, and especially if the pus reaches the intestine; and pierce it from within, and know that when it is the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small one.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines, which are called "young", cannot heal when they are raw, and this is due to the thinness of the veins through which they pass, and because of the subtlety of the whole body, and their close connection to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the vein pops out of the wound, put it back in just like the intestines, while it is fresh; and if it is old and has become green or black, you should tie up the area that is black so that bleeding does not occur, for there are veins and arteries there; then cut away what is between the thread, and hang the two ends down from the part below the wound to facilitate extraction when the vein breaks, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	of the treatment of boils
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestines are torn, and the wound is small, it can sometimes be restored in some people, for I saw a man who was pierced by a lance in the belly; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, and became inflamed and turned into a fistula, and from it came digestion and flatulence; I applied a poultice according to what I could, and did not cease to apply a caustic until he was healed, and the wounds closed.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sewing, I doubted that the patient had a malady in his belly; and he had no evil, but remained in better condition, eating and drinking; and some experimenters said that when there is a small wound in the intestine, it should be bound in such a way: take a thread from a ram's testicles, then bring together the lips of the wound, and when the thread has opened its mouth, place it over the two lips so that it tightens its mouth upon them; and then tie off the thread, and it will hold so that it cannot come undone, and then place another thread after in the same manner as before, until the wound is completely closed; and then cut the thread.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If they pierce the intestine, and no harm comes to the patient, one can sew up the intestine with a fine thread cut from an animal's bowel, in this manner: take the tip of this intestinal thread which is well-chewed, and then tie it to a fine linen thread which is wound tightly, then thread the needle, and sew up the intestine, and tie off the thread; and this method of sewing with threads is nothing other than according to the way of hope and expectation; and if the wound is large and broad, especially when it is in one of the grails of the intestines, there is no health or cure unless one uses great subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of fistula wherever it may be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it wakes up, is universally called a "fistula", and especially when it is swollen and becomes bow-shaped.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.
