And a fistula is according to its nature a hard and white knot, where there is no pain, and it is as swollen as the wing of a bird; sometimes it is clear and bow-shaped, sometimes thick, sometimes small, sometimes large; and I have already spoken about this in the division of wounds, that any wound which is not healed and has no pus is only due to one of nine causes: namely, because of the thinness of blood or body, or because of its wickedness, or because there is hard matter within, and on the edges, which does not allow pus to form; or there is too much swelling; or the site is weak, and the matter poor in quality; or the medicine used is ineffective; or the corruption is a type of pestilence; or due to the nature of the region, digestion and healing are delayed, and there is swelling; or there are veins or bones: and I have already described all these causes, their signs, and the medical treatments in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Now I must tell you about the treatment of a fistula that is done by hand.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	You should know that fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins and arteries, and nerves, in the syphilis, or intestine, or bladder, or any of the ribs, or in the spine of the back, or in any joint of the hands or feet, and even those that come to the principal part of a limb, and similar places.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that are in this way are of grief sanation, and there is nothing but labor and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come to where I have said, and you have confidence in the cure, and you see it being understood, then take an iron or copper tent, if the fistula is straight, so use it; and if the fistula is crooked, then search with a subtle thin tent of lead, for the lead bends easily around the crookedness; and if the fistula has multiple openings and you cannot search it well with tents, then catheterize through one of the openings, for moisture will pass from one opening to another, and cleanse it; then press it gently to your strength, so that you know whether there is bone or nerve, and feel how deep it goes, and ask the patient about the pain he feels when you press his hand, and where he feels it; and when you truly know the location of the fistula, if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places I have told you, then treat it as I have instructed, and remove the foreign matter and corrupted flesh that are inside; then cure the wound until it is healed, and if the fistula is very deep and straight, then you should probe deeply to your ability, then moisten tents with medicinal water, and insert them into the fistula up to its head, so that the medicine corrodes the excess matter remaining at the bottom; then apply soothing ointments to heal the flesh, until it is healed, and if it is not healed by this, then cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then probe it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerve does not trouble the principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there is decay and blackness, then treat with hot things until the decay is completely removed, then cure with healing poultices until it is healed; and if it is not healed, and returns to its previous state, know that you have not reached the bottom: then uncover and probe until you reach the bottom, and remove all the decay, then restore the place; and if it is thus healed, that is good.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the decay is too deep for you to reach; then there is no other remedy but to leave it to nature; and if there is a small corrupt bone, and you can pull it out with tweezers, then extract it with the appropriate instrument for this purpose, and if there are many bones, pull them all out, and do not leave any behind; and if moisture causes a contrary effect, and there is no error or fear, then cut and dry, and apply poultices, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then place something on the wound that encourages pus, and let it remain until the pus extends around the bone, and then the bones will come apart more easily; and if it is a large bone, such as the leg or thigh, then scrape away the rottenness only until the blackness is completely removed, and then close up the wound; and if there is a great deal of corruption, and it reaches down to the marrow of the bone, then it should be cut out and covered entirely down to the corruption, and then healed until it is closed up; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that you can take example and aid from this in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man of about 30 years old who had pain in his leg due to an internal cause, so that the matter came out in his leg, and it became swollen with a large abscess, and there was no reason to open it; but the doctors, through their folly, worked on him until the abscess opened, and much matter came out, and then it became a fistula, and many holes opened up all over his body, emitting pus and moisture from his body; and many doctors treated him for two years, and there was no wise man in the art of medicine who knew how to heal him, so I was called in, and when I saw his leg and the medicines that they were using to treat him, and what was flowing out of the holes, it caused great harm to the body; and the skin of the young man turned red, and he had a yellow complexion.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent at one of these openings, and then explored all the openings, and found that one opened into another throughout the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	So I hurried and cut into one of the openings until I exposed a part of the bone, and found it rotten and pierced all the way through; I treated what appeared to be rot on the bone, and believed there was no more rot than what I removed; and then I began to heal the wound with strong remedies for a long time, but couldn't close it; so I started over, and exposed the bone as before, and found the rot continued in the bone, which I treated, and then cut out, and worked at closing the wound; but I couldn't, no matter how much I cut around the bone, and removed all its soft tissue; then I restored it with remedies, and it healed quickly, and didn't need to reopen the wound except for the weakness of the patient who couldn't bear it, and from fear of death that I had of him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often through the blood-letting he bled profusely, but was completely healed, and a hard lump grew in the place of the bone, and he was of good disposition and had no harm or discomfort anywhere, neither when walking nor lying down.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken anywhere in the body, one should treat it thus: take a length of linen, and hold it at the end of the exposed bone, and have someone pull it upwards; and take another piece of coarser linen than the first, and tie it over the lump that is above the bone, and hold the end, so as to draw the corrupted flesh towards the bottom, and uncover the flesh above where you see the corruption, so that the string does not cut into the flesh; and put a hot iron or a wooden paddle under the bone to cover the corrupted flesh; and one should continue to do this as often as one can see and feel the corruption, and do it again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is broken and does not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in part of it, then uncover the flesh all around; then put a hot iron underneath, and then pull the sore from one side to the other, and let the poultice be applied from the long end of the corruption as we have said; and if the corruption is at the joint, then cover the corrupted joint and apply the poultice to the bone on the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuance of two joints, then there is no other way to cover it; and if the corruption is in the knuckle of the hand or the foot, then this thing is very strong, but nonetheless you should inquire into that corrosion, how it appears to you; and cleanse it in every way you can, but so that the vein or nerve do not cause any harm; and know that there are many knives and instruments for covering these bones, according to the arrangement of the bones and the appearance of them, and their thickness and thinness, and their size and smallness, and their hardness. And therefore one must prepare an instrument for each appearance of work; and know that the work will show you the instrument which you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the manners of diseases; then think about the instrument which you need according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The heads can suffer damage from internal causes or external ones; and when you have treated this corrosion with medicine, but it does not help, then you must cover the affected limb up to where the corrosion occurs, so that the patient escapes death by this, or by the greater evil of losing the limb; and the signs are that the limb becomes black, as if burned by fire, and after the blackness comes the corrosion, spreading from limb to limb, and throughout the body; so you must be quick to cover it, and if it is due to the sting of some venomous creature, such as a sea scorpion or snake, and similar, and the sting is on the head, then cover it, and do not give it any space to reach the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it reaches the hand, then cover at the joint so that corrosion does not reach the arm; and if it reaches the arm, then cover at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, that is death, and there is no remedy other than the quantity of its virtue; and thus do likewise when corrosion comes to the foot: if it comes in the first joint, then cover after the other joint; and if it comes to the foot, then cover all the foot; and if it rises in the leg, then cover at the joint of the knee; and if it comes above the knee, there is no other remedy except to cut off the limb so that the patient escapes death; and the method of covering or binding the limb is that you tie it above and below, and extend one bandage downward from one tie, and another bandage upward from the other tie, and you loosen the flesh which is between the two bandages with a wide spatula, so that the bone is exposed; then cover and bind it, and place a linen cloth on each side so that the binding does not touch the healthy area, and comes to the patient no further harm or abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if bleeding occurs when you work, cauterize the area gently, or apply some restraining powders; then return to your medicine until it is complete, then bind the injured limb with a suitable bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to a man in his sleep: he had a darkness that looked like a burn, and this corrosion first appeared on his big toe of the foot, so that it spread all over his foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, he wrapped his foot, and was healed; and long afterwards the corrosion returned on his finger, and he came to me, and I put some reflective substances on him after purifying the body, and could not stop the corrosion; and he wanted me to cut off his hand, and I did not want to, for I had no hope of removing the matter; and I also doubted that if I cut off his hand, he would die, for the strength of the man was weak; and he despaired completely, and returned to his homeland, and wrapped his hand, and was healed; and I have not told anyone about this except those who need it.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	At times an abscess forms in a fleshy area and remains so long that it causes a large gathering of pus; then it bursts and drains, leaving the site hollow, like a vessel; and the skin above is as delicate as a thin cloth, not healing up to the bone or nerve, and such a disease is called 'sore', but not 'fistula'; but if it extends so far that it reaches the bone deeply, then it is called a 'fistula'; and the skin is such that you can cover it all around, and especially when it is delicate, like a cloth; and it does not heal over because of its corrosion.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you have confidence that the skin will heal, and the corruption is not deep, and the skin is thick with flesh, then treat it with a clot-forming cautery in this way: examine whether the breast is swollen and the pus within has a foul odor; then use an Egyptian medicine made thus: take asafoetida and oil and litharge, equal parts, and melt them in a vessel over fire until the medicine turns red and becomes as thick as honey; then take some according to your need, and dilute it with water and honey, and inject it into the breast, and hold the opening closed; leave it for two hours, then remove it by squeezing; do this repeatedly until the breast is cleansed and the pus has drained; and sometimes the breast is cauterized with ash water when this medicine is not available; take vinegar ashes of vine wood, pour water over them, let stand, and use to inject; or you can cauterize with honey and wine, which makes the skin form on its own; or with other medicines and ointments, whose properties I have described in the section on ointments. And if the opening of the breast is small, and the cannula of the syringe cannot enter, then widen it slightly with a knife, and apply a tent of Egyptian ointment, or basilicon ointment, so that it may enter; and if the wound is too large, cut it open only enough for the syringe to enter, and if the opening that drains pus is above, cover it below where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Because when the bowel is perforated, you should not let any food enter it; and if you cannot cover the breast beneath as you wish, prepare in such a way that the bowel moves to the lowest place it can, for when the bowel is perforated, you should not let any food enter it, and if you cannot cover the breast beneath as you wish, prepare in this way: let the bowel move gently downward, and leave nothing of the bowel; and take consolative medicines to be placed over the wound, and have a linen cloth covering all the wound; then cover the opening of the breast more widely than before, then apply soothing ointment according to the size of the opening, and place it on the opening of the wound to ease the bowel, and do not remove the large cloth for several days; and often remove the one over the opening of the breast to remove the bowel, and test what comes out of the bowel, whether it is venom or pus or sufficient, or digested or undigested; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is an abscess or not, and when your medicine has spread in this way and you see the nature that rises over the wound, then know that the breast is healing, and approach the wound; and then loosen it in the morning, or at noon, and when you loosen the wound, change the other cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if the breast milk flows for many days, know that the breast will not dry up.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons spread slowly over a long time, do not despair of health, for health is approaching.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	Because there are people whose wounds fester for a long time due to the putrefaction of flesh in their wounds, and others who experience the opposite effect; and if milk flows from the breast slowly after many days, know that the breast is not healing; and if the breast takes a long time to heal and is distant, apply dry medicines which are moist in substance but dry in nature, such as diaφanous ointment, for it contains a large portion of vitriol, and it is the best medicine; prepare diaφanous ointment with rose oil, and rosewater equal in substance; then cook it and use it as needed; and if this ointment is not available, take myrrh, aloes, and incense, grind them into a powder and sprinkle it over the honey while it is on the fire; then glue a cloth to it and apply it to the breast, and sometimes an aristologist's long needle is used, as well as roots of celestial lilies, which are like flour and centaury; and one can use simple or composite remedies: grind them into a powder and mix with the honey as I have described, and then apply it. And if the fistula takes a long time to heal and is not cured by this treatment, know that corruption has reached the bone, causing hardening of the bones or the limbs; therefore, one should use the cure for fistulas as we have described earlier.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the nail
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that arises under the nail of the finger or toe, or occasionally elsewhere; and when it becomes infected, and no attention is paid to it, then the abscess becomes pus-filled, and it runs and seeps out as far as the root of the nail, and sometimes all the way to the bone; and corrosion reaches the bone, causing a foul odor, and the affected digit swells, and its color turns yellow.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have described in the previous section, and the treatment does not help, then you should cut away all the surplus growth from under the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cautery is a great help if the bone and nail are healthy, and the nail is growing over the flesh and starting to pierce it, and there is bleeding: in this case, you should place a thread under the nail so that the flesh is drawn up, and then carefully cut away the flesh, and apply fiery and corrosive medicines to remove all of it; then treat with ointments until it heals.
Et se li corrosion est en l’os, si le cope, et trai fuer, car tant com li os corrumpus i est, si ne puet saner; et se tu vois le doi corrumpre, si le cope en I des nous si com il est devant dit, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est ferus, et boutez, et il sent grant dolor, si covient que tu le sainnes premier; puis cope l’ungle dou spatumile agut en taillant de travers desus, et warde que li taille ne viegne jusc’a la char qui est desoz l’ungle, car li malaides sentiroit trop grant dolor; et s’il avient, si met chose sus qui apaise.	And if the corrosion is in the bone, cut it out and draw it out, because as long as the bone is corrupted, it cannot heal; and if you see it become infected, cut it open at the nail of the little finger diagonally, and be careful that the cut does not reach the flesh under the nail, because the patient would feel too much pain; and if this happens, apply something to soothe the pain.
la dolor dou sourdoit de la main	the pain from the deafness of the hand
Li dois ajostez qui naist en mains d’aucuns homes par aventure est toz charnus, et par aventure i a teil ou il a osses, et aucune fois i a ungle, et aucun d’aus naissent en la racine de la jointure, ou li naissance est en aucuns nous des dois.	The two types of nails that grow on some people's hands by chance are all fleshy, and by chance there is bone, and sometimes there is an nail, and sometimes they grow at the base of the joint, or the growth is in one of the fingers.
Cil qui naist en aucune nout dou doi ne se muet, et cil qui naist a la jointure dou doi, par aventure se muet; la taille de celui qui est charnus si est legiere, en teil maniere: taille le en sa racine d’un large spatumile.	Those who grow on the nail of the finger do not move, and those who grow at the joint of the finger sometimes move; the size of the one that is all fleshy is light, in such a way: cut it off at its root with a broad spatula.
Cil qui naist en la racine de la jointure si est grief a curer: si te tien dou coper.	He who is born at the root of the joint is difficult to cure; you must keep him covered.
En celui qui naist ou doit au derrien nout, si covient que tu copes premier la char reondement jusc’a l’os, puis cope l’os a une soie convenable a ceu, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	In the one who is born with an anal fissure, you should first cut the flesh around it roundly to the bone, then cut the bone with a suitable thread for this, then heal it until it is healthy.
Li soudemens que vient as dois ensamble vient par naissance, ou par soudement de plaie, ou par arsure de feu, ou par semblans choses.	The joints that come together come from birth, or from joining a wound, or from a burn, or from similar things.
Si couvient que tu copes celle soudeure, si que li doit repairent selonc lor formes naturelz; puis met entre dous tentes ou drapelz moilliez en oile roset, qu’il ne se soudent; ou tu met entre dous pieces de plonc subtilz, tant que li leus soit soudez, si com il covient.	Then you should cut the fissure so that the anus heals according to its natural shape; then place between two tents or pieces of wet cloth in rose oil so that it does not heal; or place between two pieces of thin lead, until the tissue is healed, as it should be.
Se soudemens vient a aucun de ses dois avec la paume, si cope celle sodure si com il covient.	If this swelling comes to either palm with the fingers, then treat this fracture as it should be done.
des vils	of the poor
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres.	Veins are large, enveloped vessels filled with melancholy superfluities that come in many parts of the body; and they occur more in legs of those who walk and work and carry things, than in others.Et sont causees par humours melancolieux et superfluitiez de sang qui montent en haut par les veines.
Il covient donques que tu li aministres aucune fois espurgement de cole, et puis le saine de la basilique.	Therefore, you should administer an emetic to him occasionally, and then cleanse him with basil water.
Li cure de fer si est selonc II manieres: l’une est c’on les cope, et traie on fuer le sanc noir; et li autre maniere si est que tu lieves la voinne, et la trai toute fuer.	The treatment of varicose veins is according to two methods: one is that you cut them, and draw out the black blood; and the other way is that you raise the vein, and draw it all out.Et si li membres sont gonflez, ou tu leves la veine selonc la maniere sus dite et tu trais le sang noir.
Li taille si est selonc ceste maniere: arose li premier la jambe d’aigue chaude mout fort, tant que li gros sans soit subtiliiez, puis estrain la jambe dou malaide des desus la cuixe jusc’a la partie desoz le genoil; puis cope la voinne en I leu, ou en II ou en III, d’une taille large, puis eslieve et trair fuer le sanc noir a ta main, des l’un chief jusc’a l’autre, tant que tant de sans en isse com li vertus dou malaide puet soffrir; et puis la lie, et li comande qu’il se teigne de viandes enjanrant cole noire; et recomence l’evacuation et la sainie quant les voinnes sont plainnes, et nuist au malaide.	The surgery is performed in this manner: first, soak the leg in very hot water until the veins are dilated, then dislocate the leg from above the thigh to the joint below the knee; next, cut the vein in one of three places, making a large incision, and then express and draw out the black blood into your hand, from one end to the other, until as much blood comes out as the patient can endure; then ligate it, and order them to apply a poultice of black koliny over the wound; when the wounds are healed, repeat the bleeding and poulticing, and let the patient rest.
Li alevemens de li est selonc ceste maniere: reis la jambe dou malaide, s’il i a mout de poil, puis le met ou bain, et li arose la jambe d’aigue chaude tant qu’elle deviegne rouge, et enflent les voinnes; et se tu n’as point de baing, si le chaufe au feu, et puis le cope endroit la voinne dou lonc au chief dou genoil, ou en la partie desoz a la cheville; puis aoevre le cuir a l’oncine, et escorche la voinne de chescune part, tant qu’ele apere quant on la sent; et on la voit rouge et noire, et quant elle entre ou cuir si semble ausi com une corde blainche; puis boute le rait desoz, tant qu’ele soit alevee dou cuir, et puis la pent a l’oncine legier, puis le cope en I autre leu ensus III dois; puis escorche le cuir sus la voinne tant qu’ele apere, puis la lieve au rais, si com tu as fait, et la pent a un autre uncine, si com tu as fait premiers; puis cope une autre taille, ou plusors se tu en as mestier, puis la lieve, et la cope au doi dou piet, puis la trai et lieve jusc’a la seconde taille; puis l’estrai de taille en taille, tant qu’elle isse toute fuer, puis la cope; et se tu ne la pues traire et lever, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil fort double, et la lie et la trai, et i boute desoz I rait, et torne ta main d’une part et d’autre, tant qu’il en isse; et garde qu’elle ne cope, car s’elle cope, si ne la puet on traire ne lever, et en vient nuisement au malaide; et quant tu l’as toute traite, si met sor le leu de la plaie laine moillie en vin et en oile roset; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The amputation is performed in this manner: elevate the leg if there is a lot of hair on it, then soak it in hot water until the veins dilate and the skin turns red and the veins swell; if you do not have a bath, heat it by the fire, and then cut the vein at the top near the knee, or in the part below the ankle; next, lift the skin around the wound to reveal the underlying tissue, and scrape away any dead tissue until it appears healthy and red, and when it is black and swollen under the skin it resembles a white cord; then insert a needle under the vein and draw out the blood by twisting your hand, being careful not to cut the vein, for if it cuts, you cannot draw out the blood and the patient will be harmed; once all the blood has been drawn, ligate the vein and cut it off. If you are unable to draw out the blood, insert a double needle under the vein and pull it through, twisting your hand from side to side until all the blood is out; then cover the wound with a pad of wool soaked in wine and rose oil, and change it daily until the wound is healed.
Et se li vis est contraite et torte et envoloupee ensamble, et ele n’est mie droite, si com nos avons dit, si covient que tu la fendes tortement, mais ne la coper mie; et la trai si com nos avons devant dit.	And if the wound is contracted and twisted and wrapped together, and it is not straight, as we have said, then you must split it crookedly, but do not cut it; and treat it as we have said before.
Li forme dou fer dont on cope la vis si est corbes, et ne trenche mie, qu’il ne cope la voinne; et est de grosse corbeure, car s’il estoit subtilz, si coperoit la voine, mais soit gros si com nos avons dit, et ci est li forme:	The shape of the iron used to split the wound should be curved, not cutting into the vein; and it should be a large curve, for if it were subtle, it would cut the vein, but it should be large as we have said, and its shape is thus:
de la voinne civile	of a civil vein.
Ceste voinne est enjanree en jambes, en chaudes parties ou il ne naist herbes ne arbre, et en terre ou il n’a point de moistor; et par aventure naist autre part qu’en jambes, et ceu avient de la porriture que vient desoz le cuir, si com il vient dedens le cors serpens et vers, enjanrez entre cuir et char.	This vein is angular in the legs, in hot places where no herbs or trees grow, and in land without moisture; and by chance it grows elsewhere than in the legs, and this happens from the pustules that come under the skin, as do snakes and worms, angling between skin and flesh.And if it comes from under the nails of hands or feet, it is a sign of death.
Et se li signes de l’encomencement de ceste voinne si est qu’il vient en la jambe une tres grans enflammation, puis se chainge li leus, et comence li voinne fors issir, ausi com une racine d’une plante.	And if the signs of the beginning of this vein are that a great inflammation comes in the leg, then the location changes, and the vein begins to come out, just as the root of a plant.
Quant li chiés apert, si covient que tu envoloupes entor une piece de plonc des une З et demi jusc’a II З., et la noe, et laisse le plonc pendant a la jambe, et totes les fois qu’il en ist point au defuer, si l’envoloupe entor le plonc, et la nowe; et s’elle est trop longe, si en cope une partie, et envoloupe le remenant, et ne la coper mie en sa racine, tant qu’elle soit toute issue; car se tu la copes, si rentre en la char, et fait venir aposteme et porriture ou leu, et male maladie; por la queil chose il covient qu’elle soit traite poc et poc jusc’a chief, et n’en remaigne rien ou cors; et est aucune fois ceste voinne quant elle est traite de V paumes de lonc, ou de X, et uns hons vint ja a moi, a cui elle issit de X paumes de long, et quant tu la copes, si boute I rais ou pertus, et la perce jusc’a fons, si que tout en isse; et soit vuidie li matiere qui est dedens, et amenistre au leu medicines enjanrans porriture aucun jor, puis le cure si com les apostemes.	When the vein is opened, you should wrap around it a piece of linen three and a half to four inches wide, and tie it, leaving the linen hanging down the leg; every time it comes out, wrap the linen around it again and tie it; if it's too long, cut off some, and wrap only the remaining part, and do not cover its root while it is still coming out; because if you cover it, it will go back into the flesh, causing an abscess and swelling on the site, and serious illness; therefore this vein should be treated little by little until it's completely out, and nothing remains in the body; sometimes this vein can be as long as 20 to 30 inches, and once a person came to me whose vein was 30 inches long; when you cover it, plug the hole or opening, and pierce it to the bottom so that everything comes out; empty the matter inside, and administer healing medicines on the site for several days, then treat it as you would an abscess.
Et aucune fois a ceste voinne mains rains, et meismement quant elle apert en la jointure dou piet, ou ou piet, et i vient mout de pertus, et dont il saut rains; cure le donques si com nos avons dit devant.	And sometimes this vein is open-ended, and especially when it opens in the joint of the foot, or the foot itself, and there comes a lot of pus out of it, and from which it rains; therefore, cure it as we have said before.
des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	of worms that grow between skin and flesh
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This disease is called "cattle disease" in our land because it often affects oxen. It is caused by a small worm that grows between skin and flesh, moving throughout the body, ascending and descending, until it breaks through the skin, and sometimes it can enter the eye and destroy it. This often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being cured and milked, it cannot be helped except when it comes to the surface: therefore, you must bind the area above and below with a strong string tightly, then scrape on top of it and milk it out; and if the worm is deep in the flesh, and you cannot remove it, then cauterize it with fire until it dies. The greatest harm it does is running into the eye as already mentioned; therefore, treat the patient with cleansing remedies for the body to remove excessive humors, and avoid foods that promote putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	of the pain that comes from windiness
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "vomiting" in our land, and it is a pain that comes to various members, and then moves from member to member; and I saw what I'm telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called to a sick woman and she showed me her arm, and I saw a small swelling on the vein of the arm; and soon after, I saw it rise up to the shoulder as quickly as anything, as bright as silver when it moves from one place to another; the pain left that spot and settled in the shoulder, and then a little later ran throughout the body, until it came to the other arm; then she told me that it was returning around the body, just as I saw it.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was very amazed at how she moved from limb to limb like this; for I had never seen this disease progress in this manner before.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	Nevertheless, I have often seen people whose pain moved from one place to another, but I didn't see it in the woman; and I thought that it was because women have dry bodies, and their veins are exposed, and that this windiness is forced out in this way, and not according to this reason in those who are delicate, and who have moist bodies and relaxed veins.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see to cure this disease, and the patient feels the pain, if it appears to you as we have said, then bind above and below tightly, and then press on until that windiness constrained in the place goes out; and cauterize the place; and if you do not see it yourself, then treat it with what expels windiness, such as foul pills, and serapin pills, and similar others.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Arrows are diverse, according to their appearances and according to the parts of the body where they land.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The variety of them is that there are some with large points, and small, and hooked, and glued; and those with two angles, and those with tongues, and those with parts; and those which break in any member break according to two manners: either in a principal member, such as brain, heart, liver, lung, spleen, intestine, bladder, and similar members.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When she falls into any of these places in the body, and you see the sign of death which I will tell you about later, then you should be wary of removing this arrow, for death comes after in many dispositions; and if this bad sign is not seen, and the arrow is not deeply embedded, then pull it out and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain is when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and there is a rupture above the brain, and scotomia, and soda, and discoloration and swelling of the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasm and loss of understanding, and vomiting of bile; and perhaps there is discharge from the nose or ears; and perhaps they lose their speech and voice; and there is moisture like pus coming out of the wound, and also bruise-like blood; and if you see these signs, then stop the treatment and pull out the arrow if it is not already.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The signs of a seizure when it occurs in the heart are that it is near the left breast, and feels as though it were pierced by a hard object, not hollow; and perhaps the seizure is silent like the pulse, and there is dark blood, and coldness and cold sweat, and syncope: then know without doubt that death is imminent.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of an arrow wound that never leaves the lung is foam coming from the mouth, and the throat swollen, and the patient's color changing, and panting heavily and seeking the cool air.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if the arrow pierces the covering of the foot, it is near the small bones; and it causes great pain and great swelling and panting; and all the limbs move from the shoulders.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if the arrow pierces the stomach, by chance some undigested food may come out of the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow pierces the gut, and no feces escape through the bowels, then there is no hope of a cure, nor in extracting the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow pierces the bladder, and urine escapes and flows out, and the patient feels great pain: know that the wound is deadly.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other members, such as the face and neck and throat and shoulder and elbow and spine of the back and hip and thigh and legs, and similar members, are safe according to various dispositions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in a nerve or artery, and it is not venomous, as I will tell you so that you may do likewise.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	Once there was a woman who had a seizure in her jaw, so I tested it and pulled it from under the ear fat on the other side, and she recovered without fainting.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And I treated a man with a seizure that hit him in the fat of his ear below the cartilage, and the seizure was retracted, and all I could touch was the tip towards the stem, and the seizure was as large as a Turkish bowstring, but thin at the end without ears; he recovered and no ill effects occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	I extracted an arrow from a Christian's throat; it was an Arabic arrow with ears. I cut the barbs and pulled gently until I extracted it, and the Christian was healed.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	I extracted an arrow from a man's throat, which had pierced his abdomen, and I thought he would die; but after thirty days, his condition did not worsen. So I cut the arrow, and wrapped it, and pulled it out, and he had no ill effects.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if you see a person with an arrow in their back, and the wound is sewn shut on top; and the arrow remains inside, and his natural functions are unchanged, and he experiences no discomfort in any of his natural processes:
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I saw another man, who had an arrow in his face, and the wound was sewn shut; and he remained like that without suffering great pain; and there are many other similar cases.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And there was an arrow shot into the home of the prince the king, who had a very painful toothache, and he was a little inclined to the right side; and the arrow was all swollen I was called to the cure after it had been three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very narrow.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I applied a very subtle poultice to it, and did not feel anything; but he felt a piercing and pain below his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I placed an astringent and digestive poultice on the site to prevent swelling; and the tip of the arrow appeared to me.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I continued to apply the poultice for several days, and the wound healed directly, and the pain remained for a long time, as long as he felt the arrow inside his tooth; and he told me so.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied a corrosive medicine to the wound for several days until it was open and I probed it and felt the head of the arrow which was lodged in the wound; then I treated the opening with the medicine until the head of the arrow appeared clearly; the wound healed well within four months, and then I lanced the wound and pulled out the arrow with tweezers, and it would not come out; so I continued to treat the wound with various instruments until one day I was able to pull it out with specially made tweezers, as described in this chapter, and I closed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And some believe that the cartilage of the nose cannot be restored; so I restored it, and the wound was closed and the patient fully healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Here I have told you the quality of the extraction of some arrows, so that you may apply your treatment to what I do not mention, for books cannot encompass everything; but wise masters make do with very little, and with what is present and lacking, they devise new methods and new instruments, in the descent of strange things that occur in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows strike the members in which they are lodged in two ways: either through the place where they entered or through another part; and those that go out through the place where they entered are arrows entering into fleshy parts, and sometimes they go out now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not go out now, then leave it as long as the flesh around it becomes putrid and the opening becomes enlarged; and if it is lodged in the bone and cannot come out, then leave it for several days, moving it every day; and then it will come out, and if it does not, then pierce through the bone all around with a very thin instrument until the opening around it becomes enlarged, and then pull it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is lodged in the bone of the skull, and goes just to one of the ventricles of the brain, and some of the accidents which I have mentioned appear in the patient: then do not extract it, but let it be until it becomes even after a few days, for if the arrow reaches the brain, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is lodged only in the bone and does not reach the brain, and the patient remains for a few days without any bad accident, then treat it with the instrument for extraction.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is very loose and cannot come out, then administer cauteries around it as I have told you, then cleanse the area once it has healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is lodged deep in the body so that you cannot see it, then probe it throughout with a long instrument; and if you feel it, extract it with a suitable instrument; but if because of the tightness of the wound and the depth of the arrow there is no bone or vein or tendon, then cut it as far as the wound is large; and if there are ears on the arrow by which it holds, bend or twist them so that you can extract it; and be careful not to break the arrow as you pull it out.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot remove it in one go, then leave it until the surrounding tissue has swollen; then pull it out, for the extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding makes it contrary, then apply what we have said about the cure in its chapter; and beware of the incision of the nerve and of the vein, and put in the oil as you can move the arrow without peril, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and put the patient according to the way he was when the arrow fell into him, for that is his greatest help. And if you cannot, then put it according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	Arrows that come from elsewhere, or where something has appeared from him, or the skin is swollen in such a place that one sees or feels it apparently: cut above, as far as the pincers can reach, and then pull it out; if it will not come out now, cut higher.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, then rotate your hand roundly, as far as it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it out.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it will not come out, then leave it, and try to pull it out again until it comes out; and if the arrow is in him, insert it all the way into him; and if the arrow is short, and you see that there is room for an instrument, then insert a chewed instrument so that the point of the arrow enters into the gum of the instrument; and then pull it out, and if the arrow is chewed, insert the instrument with its point entering in, to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow has touched it, you must cut all the flesh around where the venom is, if you can, then treat the wound as it should be.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the arrow pierces the foot, or leg, or stomach, or bladder, or side, and it is near the surface, and you can cut above it; and you must be careful not to cut into the vein and nerve, and then pull it out, and then stitch the wound, if necessary; and treat it until it heals.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of forceps for treating arrows is similar to an owl's beak; see the shape here:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	There are many types: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape of the feathered end is also like the feather of a bird, to push onto the tip of the arrow, just as it is shaped:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the form of the tongs for pulling and probing is as follows:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the common body vessels
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins from which one can be bled, and there are XVI in the head, namely: II batants which are behind the ears, which are called the two "ear-beaks"; and the II arteries which are in the II temples, apparent; and II veins that are in the II eyelids of the II eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is in the middle of the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the II windpipes which are in the neck; and the II veins that are above the lips, at the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich"; and the II veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which we commonly bleed are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, which is on the left side of the chest, and the common people call it "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called "fast", and is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and the common people call it "vein of the heart"; and the basilic is on the right side of the chest, and the common people call it "vein of the belly", and it is above the fossa, and is that from which we bleed, which opens clearly above the pubic bone.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the salvatella is the vein that is between the auricular and the ring finger, and it has two branches; and in the leg and in the foot there are three veins: one is below the curve of the pubic bone on the left side of the chest, and the second is superficial at the ankle on the right side of the chest; and the vein that is called  "nesse", which is at the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins below those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The bleeding of veins that are behind the ears is helped by old catarrhs and by bleeding; and the qualities of the bleeder, as I told you, and it is that you press the head of the patient, and rub the area where the veins are with a rough cloth; then squeeze the patient's neck with a vise, until the two veins appear behind the ears in two places depending on the head; then grab them with your fingers, and feel the pulse under your fingers, and sign it; then take the lance, and pierce it under the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand over the entire vein upstream, and pierce both the skin and the vein well through the two sides, and make the blood come out until you see it; then stop it and tie it, until it is healed; and I have already spoken of the incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The bleeding of the two arteries in the temples is useful for treating old-age migraines, and eye problems, and tears in the body; and the quality of the bleeding is as I have said: and it is that the patient stretches his neck so that the two veins are clearly visible; and feel the pulse under your thumb, and then sign with your finger; then lift the skin above the vein at the top of your thumb, and insert the needle underneath, and lift the vein from above, and suck out the blood according to your need; then release the patient, and put your finger on the vein for an hour, then cotton wool; and then bind it tightly, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken of their binding and extraction at the beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The bleeding of the vein on the forehead is as good as the bleeding of the cephalic in old diseases of the face, and for migraine and redness; and its quality is that the patient twists his neck until the vein appears; then take the instrument called "fosseur", whose shape is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point over the vein and press with your hand or something else and let the blood flow according to the amount you see; then release the neck of the patient, and tie the vein until it is healed, and sometimes the operation is done with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Nevertheless, the flax threads should not be too thin, and the wound should be stitched across, for the bone is near, and it may break the flax thread when it is fine.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The bleeding of the two veins in the two temples helps with migraines, and redness and eye pain, and diseases of the face; and the quality of their bleeding is that the patient twists his neck by means of some thread, as before; then he bleeds, and the bleeding should be through a short length of flame, a little wide, for there is no flesh.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, perhaps they will break; then let blood, as much as you need, and then bind it on cotton, and tie it well.
