Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The vein of the nose is good for ague, and for sudden madness, and for facial illnesses, such as emigration and redness that comes to the face, and especially when it is old; and the quality of the vein is such that the patient squeezes his neck, then his nose with your left hand, and takes a long, slender flame, and inserts it into the lip in the space between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open well otherwise, and the blood will begin to flow now; and do not go too deep, and let the blood flow according to your need, then tie it off for one night, for it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The vein of the two testicles helps with strangulation of the groin, and at the beginning of mastitis, and many illnesses, and impetigo, and corrosion, and herpes, and hemorrhoids; and the quality of the vein is such that the patient squeezes his neck from side to side as we have said; and let the master stand above the patient's head while he sits on a chair, then open the vein of the long one somewhat widely, then draw the blood temperately, or as much as is needed; then do the same in the other vein, then untie the ligature, and gently squeeze both veins so that the patient does not choke; and leave it until the morning so that the wound can heal.
de la sainie des leivres	of bleeding from the lips
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The bleeding of the veins in the lips helps with cold in the mouth, and corruption of gums, and splitting of lips, and toothache and earache.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of bleeding is that the patient should sit before you and press his neck as I have said; then turn the lip and look at two veins, one on each side, which can be recognized because they are black, and because there are small black veins around them: grab both of these, and if you cannot recognize them and you doubt their location, then grab the largest one in each area. Also, do the same for the two veins above and below, as it is a similar method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	And so also for bleeding under the tongue:
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The bleeding of the veins under the tongue also helps after bleeding from the head; it aids in tightness of the throat and diseases of the throat, mouth, and the tongue. The method for bleeding is that the patient opens their mouth before the sun, lifts their tongue, and you should see a black vein on each side: grab both of these, but do not go too deep, as arteries are located there as well.de la sainie des piere
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	Veins of the head from which one commonly bleeds are bled in two ways: either with a needle to all the broad vein of mirtin, or with a subtle olive-wood needle as sharp as a trenchant, and is called 'anesil'; and they are broad and subtle according to the breadth and narrowing of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the needle is very important, and it should be wide as you can see:
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is necessary to open the flat veins of the head that contain apparent thick blood and thick troubled blood; and that is the form of the olive-wood needle:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more pointed and delicate, and is for bleeding delicate veins that contain subtle yellow blood.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The basilic vein, which is one of these veins, helps diseases that are below the throat, and in the neck, and in the chest, and in the abdomen; and the bleeder must bleed copiously, and guard against the artery that is beneath.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it pierces the artery and bleeding occurs, then it must be staunched, as I have said; and the needle must not be piercing, but cutting like an 'anesil'.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basil does not open clearly, then you should stretch it and change to another; or you want some of it, or you heal in its place the vein in the arm: it opens clearly; and the flame copes with silence, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you want to know the place of bleeding, then you should stretch the arm so that you feel the pulse; then sign the place with ink, and then tie the arm, and copes the vein with flame silenced; and be careful not to pierce the artery when you see the place puffed up, for it is the artery: avoid it therefore.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it rising like the urine of a child, and the blood is red and thin, know that it is the blood of the artery: hasten therefore, and put your finger on it for a long time, then remove your finger if the blood stops, which often happens; tie the arm, and leave it thus, and do not move the patient; and let him be in fear, and do not move him until he is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If the blood is not staunched and it escapes, and you do not have any medicine available, then press on the artery to close it, for that is where the blood comes from; and then staunch the blood.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a strip of bark from a fig tree, and split it, and take one half and bind it well until the next day; if the bleeding stops, that is good; but if not, then stop it as we have said, with powders that stop bleeding; and the stopping of the bleeding is not harmful in many conditions because of the small size of the wound and the strength of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The bleeding from the vein in the middle helps it to draw blood from the head above and the body below, because it is made of basil and cedar, as we have said; and the surgeon must be careful not to cut too deeply, and he should find the nerve underneath, and if he cuts it too much, the wound will inflame and the nerve may be damaged, and perhaps cannot heal; and this nerve often opens up, and if it does not open in some men because of its subtlety, then you must stop the bleeding with a cautery before you touch the nerve; and guard the nerve as best you can.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, they will cut it longways.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The vein of the head if it aids, draws blood from the head and aids the eyes; and one should open it with a flame of olive oil or a flame of myrtle, for it is the safest of all veins, for there are no nerves or arteries underneath it.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	Nevertheless, one should seek the lightest vein, and not worry if one misses the first time, and try again; and by chance, the places may swell in some men when they miss the first time, but it does no harm.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bleeding depends on your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you should know about bleeding is that it is done only to maintain health and prevent illnesses; and bleeding should be done in one of the three veins: the cephalic, the fast, and the basilic; and one should bleed at the beginning of Lent, and in autumn and winter after eating, when the signs of repletion are apparent; and one should bleed on the first day or the third, after two or three hours of the day.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The bleeding that is administered for illnesses has no set time, but when the need arises during the day or night, at all times and throughout the year; and one should not bleed children until they are 14 years old, nor women who are pregnant beyond the fourth month until the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	Nor should those over 60 years old be bled.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when one wishes to bleed, in whatever manner, one should first loosen the intestines with a gentle enema if they are constipated and retaining much feces, so that the veins do not draw harmful excess fluids from the intestines to the principal limbs; nor should one bleed those who are very bloated from food, or intoxicated, until they have digested their food, nor those who are suffering from diarrhea, vomiting, abdominal discharge, excessive sexual intercourse, or exertion from work, watching, fasting, and anything else that weakens the body, either through the use of weapons or by illness; then gently purifies the humors with food, drink, and medicine if you have the ability; then enter a bath if nothing else can be done to purify the blood, and bleed from the vein at the base of the penis around the third hour, as we have said; and abstain from exertion that day, as well as from pain, lust, and similar activities; and let the bleeder be higher than the one being bled, and rub the arm two or three times, then tighten the ligature above the vein gently, for if it is too loose or too tight, it will not affect the blood; then rub the site with the hand until the veins swell and can be felt; then moisten the blade of the lancet with a little old oil, then place his thumb from his left hand over the vein below the site where he wishes to bleed, so that the vein does not slip or slip under the blade.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that flow like cords to the wound, and some that are full of wind, so that when one puts a flame to them, they withdraw from the flame and cannot open the vein, and thus one is made of these; and if the wound is opened, the wound is too narrow, so the surgeons must be careful in such cases.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens the first time, that is good; if not, then try again a little lower on the leg or arm, if the limb is not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the vein is swollen and the patient is afraid, leave it for a day or two without binding the arm: perhaps there will be an abscess; nor enter the bath, then resume the phlebotomy if she pleases; and if the orifice is small, cut through the skin very gently and you doubt that it does not flow so much blood as you wish, then apply the flame directly to that orifice itself; and work gently, thus the vein will be swollen; for this happens many times when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the area swollen, do not re-bandage the wound, and instead apply a little liniment of oil, for it lightens the body of blood, and in this place the oil is changed into liniment; and thus administer the liniment of oil in every bandage that you bandage veins, to stop the flow of blood; and it also makes triaicled bowels when applied to the area; and subtly the blood disperses when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if a large abscess comes, which often happens, especially when the opening of the vein is small, and the blood issue is slight, then be quick, and apply to the area a sponge dampened in warm water and salt, and compress it for an hour; and you must do this after the flow of blood from the vein, and if it remains on the spot for several days, a blackness or green color appears, it does him no harm; and if you see any swelling, apply something of aloe or myrrh made into a poultice, ointment, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And often there is an abscess and a appearance of swelling at the site of the basilic vein; therefore, put your hand on it, and if you feel the area soft to the touch when compressing with your hand, then that swelling is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Therefore be sure not to place anything on the sky that we have said, because it can go without from the artery; but make a dry plaster to harden the area, then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is healed.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And treat each bleeding according to its quantity and the color of the blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	Because if the blood is black, let it flow until it turns red; and if you see it thick, let it flow until it becomes thinner; and if it is too hot, let it cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is necessary for one who is full and swollen, and needs bloodletting, that one makes them a larger wound, and the flames should be wide; and for one who is weak, do the opposite, and they must be bled little and often, and one should bleed them by cutting across, not puncturing; and this method of bleeding is safe from blood loss and nerve damage, and is better than bleeding from a long or large wound.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for one whose body needs bleeding, one should give them moist bread in pomegranate juice; if they are hot, then draw out blood three or four times. And if they are of a cold complexion, then eat before the bleeding moist bread in mulled syrup, or in aromatic honey syrup with spices like pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a well-scented syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he faints after the loss of a lot of blood, then he should drink some warm broth and sweet-smelling syrup, and use other things that we have mentioned in the chapter on fainting, for the opening of a vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he wants to open his arm and bleed again, then when he is weakened by significant bleeding, he should bleed a little at a time according to the amount of his continued strength.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever wants to open his arm after the first bleeding and he has a strong body, then let him bleed at .VII. hours after the first bleeding or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever wants to bleed elsewhere, they should bleed on the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is a lot of blood inside the body which has been heated, and it causes fever; so you must draw out a large quantity, and widen the hole until it bleeds freely; then you should check all the conditions of bleeding, and put your hand on his pulse when he is bleeding, so that death does not come in the place of the wound, and this happens many times when the bleeding person is negligent; and you must not press hard when you see the arm loosening and the blood flowing out a second time, and the hole is closed, but you should put your hand on it gently; nor if it is crooked, should he stretch his arm suddenly, for that would be bad; but let him keep still until he bleeds again a second time; then you can touch it with the tip of a flame, so that the congealed blood at the hole of the vein melts away, and put some hot water on it, and press gently.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein is swollen, let it be so, and do not constrict it until the abscess has subsided.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if it is necessary to bleed again a second time, then open the vein in the same place, or another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The veins in the arms are bled in the area of the main vein because it is composed of smaller veins.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the method of bleeding is that the patient immerses his hand in hot water until the vein turns red; then he should be bled slowly, so that the vein appears clearly, and then he should be bled through the middle, not from the side or from above; and the incision should be wide, and bleeding should be done close to the joint of the hand, and if blood does not come out, then put the hand back in hot water and let the blood flow into the water until you have enough; and if it is winter, do not put the hand back in hot water, for it is put in there more in winter than in summer; and bleeding from this vein is safer than from any other vein, as there are no arteries or nerves.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	Bleeding from the vein of the right little finger is beneficial for all diseases of the liver, and here is how it is done: stretch out the hand, and immerse it in hot water until the vein swells up, so that one can see it; then bleed it through the middle, and if you cut it across, it will do no harm; and do not cut too deeply, for the nerves are completely naked under the skin; then put the hand back in hot water if the blood has congealed in the wound and none comes out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is necessary, then put oil and bandages on the vein to heal quickly, and do likewise for each vein.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The bleeding in the left hand is good for the disease of the mumps, and do everything just as I told you about the right side.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The sauce of the sophia is good for all diseases that are underneath the body, such as diseases of the bowels, and retention of flowers, and disease of the kidneys, and of the hips and old legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the qualities of its sauce are such that the patient puts his foot in hot water, and rubs on the vein until it perishes, and ties over the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and up the foot they go a lot of rains; heal it therefore at the widest rain, or at the ankle, whichever moves best.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal it on the foot, then guard against the nerves that are underneath, and heal it across as in chopping; and let the flames be extinguished.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if the blood cannot issue, then immerse the foot in water and let the vein drain well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the healer fails the first time, he should start again the second time higher up, for the place is salty; and do not be afraid of nerves, as we have said, and likewise make the Sophia on the other foot equally.Et si li sainier ne peut le sainier si haut, qu’il face en bas de la jointure dou piet, car il n’i a pas de nerf, si com nos avons dit; et s’il n’est au piet, qu’il face a la cheville ou au rain, selon comme li voinne se muent le plus.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The location of the sciatic vein is at the ankle bone, and its pulse corresponds to the pain in the hip when there is hot blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of its healing is such that the patient goes into the bath, and twists above the ankle IIII turns, for otherwise the vein does not open; and if it opens, then heal it in every way you can, and by crossing over; and it is better that you cover it, for the place is safe, and it is very relaxing for most people.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not drain it, then heal any vein that opens on the back of the foot, and towards the little toe, and be careful of the nerves; and make the blood flow as much as you see fit, and then loosen the ligature, and place cotton on top and hold it tightly; it is now healed.
des sainies de ventouse	of cupping.
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Cupping glasses are made from horns, or brass, or glass; and cupping is done according to two methods: either by cutting and drawing blood, or without cutting.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this cupping which is done without bleeding is done in two ways: with or without fire; and the cupping that is done by bleeding and by extraction of blood is performed at 14 places on the body, one of which is in the middle of the head; and another in the neck; and two more on either side of the neck; and a cupping jar under the chin; and two more on the shoulders; and two more on the buttocks; and two more on the thighs; and two more on the calves; and a cupping jar on each ankle; and the cupping does not treat any blood except for small veins that are scattered in the flesh, and because of this it does not weaken at all, as is done with bleeding; and it should not be administered, neither with fire nor without, in any disease that comes from fullness, until the whole body has been emptied.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if by necessity of illness it is necessary to bleed, or due to habits, then we shall bleed each hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and among them and in every time; for there are some who, when they need to bleed, have a heavy head; and there are some who experience fullness and redness in their face, and in their head, and neck, and darkness in their eyes; and some who experience a drop of blood in their mouth, and have a swollen tongue, and bleed; and there are those who dream, and see through the night blood and wounds and similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	And when we see these signs, and especially when it is during the full moon, we command them to bleed after three hours of the day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	Bleeding from the nose helps with headaches ... that comes to the eyes, and it should not be after the evacuation of the whole body; and this ventilation is in the place of bleeding from the head, and one who has a cold complexion or catarrh should not use it, for it does them great harm; and so the elderly should not use it, nor those with cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are often bled should become unconscious, and so one should place the leech further down due to the fear of oblivion.Et si li maux sunt de la sainie de la cephalique, si convient mettre la ventouse en leu de la sainie de l’estomac, ou de la sainie du coeur, ou de la sainie des reins, ou de la sainie des poumons.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventilation in the neck is located at the junction of the neck and basilic veins, and because of this, it helps with swelling in the feet, and splitting of the channels of the lungs, and with congestion and fullness; and one should not press on it too hard, for if it is pressed too firmly, it can cause injury to the stomach and heart.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventilation at the level of the second rib in the neck helps with headaches, and eye pain and inflammation, and with strangulation, and tooth pain, and is located where the basilic vein drains; and you should instruct the surgeon to express his hand while placing it so that he does not compress the artery and cause bleeding.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	Ventilation under the chin is beneficial for diseases of the mouth, and gum corruption, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is located in the veins of the two lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	Ventilation at the armpits is beneficial for diseases that arise from heat and fullness.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The ventilation in the armpits is like three veins in the arm, as it draws blood from these large veins; and instruct the surgeon not to pierce too deeply, for the area is naked of flesh, and underneath are nerves and arteries.Li ventosation dou chief si vaut a toust et a repletion des pormons, et a dolors de dent, et est en leu de la sainie dou pis, et li dolors del col; et covient que tu comandes qu’il ne fere mie trop em parfont, car il y a ners et arteres.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The cupping glass placed on the back is useful for hemorrhoids and diseases underneath, and it must be large, made of brass, and well-made; and if it is too thin, it may break and cause large wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	Cupping glasses on the legs heal very well, as they draw blood from throughout the body, and are effective for old pains in the joints, and in the hips, and in the bladder, and they relieve swelling; they are located at the .ij. sophenes, and the .ij. ankles, and they weaken the body after a long time, and bring about fainting in various conditions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of applying the cupping-glass is to place it first empty, and draw gently, and apply it firmly, and move it evenly, and do not cease doing this until you see the part become red and swollen, and the blood appear; then stop, and remove the cups, and take care in dealing with the body, for there are those who have thin skin and large pores: therefore one should only strike once, and make large wounds, and a little deep; and suck gently.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if the blood is thick, one should strike twice: the first time to open the way for the thick blood.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if the blood is very thick, one should strike a third time; and when we want to draw blood little by little, we only need to strike once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want a lot of blood, we bleed often; and if the blood is thick, we pierce it with a needle, and the end is that the heart is pierced suddenly, and it suits those who have thick and tough skin and narrow pores, that you grease the ends of the cups with aperitif and dissolutive oil: if it is in summer, with violet oil, or almond oil, or squash seed oil; and if it is in winter, with watercress oil, or lily, or camomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the person has a gross and cold surplus, take oil of wormwood, or of balsam, or aniseed oil, and similar oils.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if those who are bled have tender skin and large pores, no oil should be used, but they should be washed after cupping with rose water, or cold water, or mulberry water, or squash water, or porcelain water, or similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And those who have a lot of moisture, if they rise from aspen, or myrtle water, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have large superfluities should rise from old wine, or from pure water, or from a decoction of anise or camomile, or other similar things; and one should not bleed with a cupping glass before the bath or em bath, but after the bath for an hour or two; and one should not sleep after venting, and it is necessary that he should warm himself when he is to be bled and when he has been bled.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And guard against those who are bled being constipated, and if the blood is too sharp and inflamed; one should then eat cold things like pomegranates, endives, lettuce with garlic, and similar things; also drink little, and eat the meat of young birds, and moist foods.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those of a cold complexion should drink honey syrup, and moderate old wine, and young, and eat soup, and the meat of young birds and pigeons; and on the day that one is bled, one should drink more than eat; and it is fitting to give some people treacle or musk before bleeding, or after, to strengthen the principal members; and warm the blood, but those of a hot complexion should not drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The cupping glasses that are placed to cause bleeding are those placed on the liver, and on the mumps, and on the gout, and on the belly and the belly and the thighs and the hips, because these members do not endure being hurt under the eyes, and it is not done except to attract blood from one member to another, as we put it on the breasts when the nipples are healthy; to remove the viscosity that is in the member, as we place cupping glasses on the belly and on the belly to make the member smaller; and it removes pain when there is congestion or stone, or perhaps the congestion, or desert the stone from its place; and so does she when one is placed on the liver and on the mumps when there is retained flatulence, and these cupping glasses are administered empty to suck only; and sometimes they are administered together with fire, and sometimes filled with warm water, as in diseases of the pleurisy, and in such a way one fills the cupping glass with hot water alone, or with water in which suitable herbs have been cooked for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the fire cupping is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And it has a width of two inches and a half palm deep, and on the side around the middle there is a small hole, as well as to push a needle, and it is made of bronze, smooth in front so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle there is a crossbar of bronze or iron, to place a candle, and they are both large and small according to the diseases and the age of those who take them; for the ventouses of children are different from the old, and of the thin from the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And you should thus place this ventouse on the limb: take the candle of wax or the linen, and put it inside the ventouse through the bar in the middle of the ventouse, so that the flame is at the bottom of the ventouse so that it does not burn the patient; then put it on the limb, and you must place your fingers over the hole we mentioned, so that when one wishes, the vapor can go out, and remove the ventouse; and take the linen as before, and repeat it often if necessary.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	Therefore the cupping glass which is administered for pleurisy, for all aquosity, has neither rod nor perforation, and is not released until it is full of water, and is placed on the limb only in this way; and that is its form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Leeches are not released until in members where one cannot place cupping glasses due to their smallness, such as lips and gums, and similar places; and in bare flesh, such as toes or nipples, and others like them; and the quality of their use is that when you find leeches that are in clean, fresh water without any foreign matter, take them; and put one into fresh water, until they become familiarized, and do not move around; then cleanse the vein with a cut and cupping, then rub the member until it turns red, and place the leeches on top; and when they are full and stick, if it is a place where one can apply cupping, then do so, for it is much better.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then raise the area with ash, and then with water, very well, and then compress it; and if the bite is too low on the body of the leech, moisten a linen cloth in cold water, and place it over the bite until the leech is suffocated; and if there are many leeches, place ground vitriol, or gall, and similar things, over the area until they are suffocated; or place half a handful of peeled beans over the area and leave them until they turn red on the spot, and it will now stop bleeding; and if you need more, take other leeches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the leeches will not attach, then rub the area with fresh blood, or prick it with a needle so that some blood comes out, and then place them over the area, and as soon as they smell the blood, they will attach; and when you see that they are defecating, sprinkle powdered aloe and salt, or ashes, over them, and they will stop now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here begins the book of fractures.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and it is a remedy for fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, dear son, that the foolish people wonder at this chapter, which they have never seen in any of the ancient books, nor have they read any letters; and for this reason, science is strange in our land, for I have never found any good ones; and I know nothing about them, except through the science of the ancient books, in which I have studied so much that I have acquired knowledge, and through experience and the habit of my life. And I have described to you in this chapter what is contained in it, and I have abbreviated it at the end, and I have clearly shown the forms of the instruments that are used, as I have done in the two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, we should say in the prologue of this book the sum of its contents and the chapters in which the wise man places his understanding, and dwells upon its truth, so that those who are experienced may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when a fracture or dislocation or torsion or break occurs in someone, you must hurry to treat the patient from both sides, if nothing else prevents it, such as weakness of the body, or youth, or old age; and if the weather is not very hot or too cold; and eat cool foods, namely cold joints, and bird and deer meat, and drink no wine, nor eat any greasy foods, and do not fill yourself too much with food that fills the veins with blood, until you have a doubt about a hot abscess or an outbreak of material in the limb; then let the patient return to his former regimen.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, one should feed the patient foods that promote swelling, or that have viscosity, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and testes, and feet, and cow's stomach, and offal, and fresh fish, and wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For with much swelling the fracture is reduced more quickly.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of the old and decrepit cannot be well healed or joined according to their nature due to the dryness of the limbs, nor those that are too tender, such as the bones of small children; but have no fear, reset the broken bone, using the large tendons which stretch and join the limb together, so that it is forced into its former position; and do not stop at any point in his work, and for this reason, one should eat lots of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And you should know that fractures can occur in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For a fracture of the head is different from a fracture of the foot, or leg; and I will tell you in this chapter all kinds of fractures.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a fracture that goes to the bone, and another in crushing, like the crack in a quill used for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And there is a fracture with a wound, and a complete fracture is a clean break.Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And in every way, there is its own method and proper instrument for restoration, according to what the memory brings to mind; and the fracture of the bone is known by its being twisted, and clearly apparent by touch, and sounding when pressed with the hand; and if there is no twisting or feeling in the touch, and the patient does not feel great pain, then there is no fracture; but it can have twisting, or splitting, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	You must not move it with your hand, but apply remedies that come later, and then hold it still very gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And you should know that the fracture that goes into the bone, and the two parts are separated, they must now be set equal, so that hot abscesses come; and if cold abscesses come, let it rest for a day, until the abscess is relieved; then set it equal to the move that you can make easily and without bleeding, and know that the restoration of this one is easier than the restoration of the one with pieces; then constrict it as it should be done afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if in the bone there are broken pieces, whether it is in two parts, whether it is hand or foot, or a small member, or on two strings, or on one string and your hand; and set the member according to its natural shape, so that when the parts of the broken member are separated, you bring them back together by all means into their places as you can, and be careful that your work does not cause injury or pain to the patient; and join the two heads of the bones well according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it with your hand if it seems to you that it is not well aligned; then adjust it properly, and do not pull or press too hard, as those who cause hot abscesses and contractions in the limb by their treatment, as we have seen many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is at its worst, then treat the patient well so that he does not move it, whether waking or sleeping, turning or otherwise; and be sure that the member is so secure that he feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when he feels no pain, then it is not at its worst, and you should put him in such a position that he feels no pain; and be careful that he is placed straight so that no crookedness comes to it when it is restored; and the qualities of the broken member are according to what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that broken members vary in smallness and size and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Because there are small members, such as arms and legs and the like: these should be wrapped with soft, thin linen; and for larger ones, such as thighs and legs, use a wide, strong bandage, for wide bandages embrace the whole large member and constrict it from all sides equally so that there is no swelling; then wrap around it light bandages, three or four times according to the member, and tighten your hand a little on all of the bandage, then go above the break and tighten less, so that the break moves away a little; then soften the bandage little by little, until you grasp most of the healthy area, then take another bandage, and wrap around again over the broken area; then go to the part below the break, and tighten gently, not too tightly or too loosely, as we said above in the first hour; then put between the bandages linen or bandages, so that they are all even, then tie it all up with a bandage on top, and then put your splints well-made on top, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, place something hot that soothes the abscess and reduces the swelling for a few days; then strain it over a fire, and let it be of medium thickness, made from a cane, or wood used for making clubs, or palm fronds, and let it be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	but the splint that is placed on the fracture should be a little thicker and wider than the others; and it should be as long as necessary for the size of the member, small or large; then strain it over the fire as before, then bind it with a thread appropriately, as in the first instance above the fracture; the tighter it is bound, the better; and the thread must be medium thickness, not too thin nor too thick, and made of soft flax; for if the threads are thick, as I have seen fools make their bandages with cords of twisted flax, this is a great error, for the bandage cannot be even if it is too thin, and there should be no less than two fingers' width between each splint.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is raw under the splints after the dislocation, then put beneath them flax or lambswool, so that it does not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a fracture, and the hernia is broken, I will describe the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And you should not extract all the broken bones on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	Because when the member is swollen, one should not put a poultice on it until after five or seven days, or more depending on the nature of the abscess and the heat that arises from it; and here is the way of ancient poultices to restore fractures, dislocations, and twists: take flour that is found on the walls of the mill, and cook it with an abundance of eggs, and apply this preparation, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it. This is the common way of the poultice that restores fractures in various situations, and especially in women and small children, because it is not too hot nor too cold.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster that restores broken bones and dislocation and twisting: take 3 parts each of elderberries, ladanums, aniseed and asafoetida, and gum arabic; myrrh and aloes, each 5 parts; alechi 8 parts; grind them into powder and mix with egg white. If the person's complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it is of good composition, and it restores broken bones until they heal, and benefits many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another way of poultice that is good for twists: take myrrh and viscum album, each 10 drams; myrrh and aloes, each 9 drams; açaç 6 drams; Armenian bole 10 drams, and grind well, and cook with water or an abundance of eggs, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of plaster for joints and bones displaced from their places, and to soothe the resulting pain, and for fractures: take new lamb's wool, and moisten it in oil and cook it, and apply it to the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	This plaster does not restore, but it is good for soothing hot abscesses and removing pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method of plaster that restores broken bones: take dry fig leaves and deadnettle leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster out of it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of plaster for the restoration of fractures and to reduce swelling from an abscess: take equal parts honey and vinegar, cook in oil, and apply it to the affected area.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take the root of mallows, chamomile, violets flowers, and wheat flour, in equal parts; grind them and cook with wine, and if the member is scalded, cook with coriander water or water, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another stronger method of plaster for when there is a tough abscess in the restoration of a member: take equal parts of honey, vinegar, and oil; cook them, strain, and apply it to the affected area. It also helps with fractures and dislocations.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the roots of comfrey, and flax seed, borage, milk thistle, and dandelions, and flowers of violets and chamomile; of each take one part. Crush them, and cook with salted water, or fresh water, or wine, depending on the heat of the member, and its condition.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Hypochares says in his book that one should not put anything on the broken member except to restore it with a cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else, and that it be kept between two things, neither too soft nor too hard.Quant l’homme ou la feme est prestes a la mort, et sent le corps fraich et colde, et ne se remue plus, prene une foye et li foyez les culles, et le cul de la foye metez sus li petiz orifices qui sont en haut li corps, si com est entre li coudes, sus li poilz de la teste, sus li petiz orifices qui sont pres l’ombelice; et les culles li metes sus li petiz orifices qui sont pres li codres.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems that Galen says that one should put on the broken member, to restore it, dry things that are slightly warm, such as myrrh and aloe and incense, and similar things, as we have said.Quant l’homme ou la feme est prestes a la mort, et sent le corps fraich et colde, et ne se remue plus, prene une foye et li foyez les culles, et le cul de la foye metez sus li petiz orifices qui sont en haut li corps, si com est entre li coudes, sus li poilz de la teste, sus li petiz orifices qui sont pres l’ombelice; et les culles li metes sus li petiz orifices qui sont pres li codres.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of ointment that is good for injury and pain: take mugwort and human hair, or bird feathers, and bee's wax, and mix them together, and grind them, and make an ointment from it and apply it.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then loosen it a little after, and take care that the patient does not feel any pain, nor is the bone moved from its place; if not, loosen it with your hands again in a few days. And if pain comes to the site, or itching, without rest or swelling, hurry up and loosen it, and remove the ointment immediately; and take light cloth, and sponge of sea moistened, and dip it in water, and raise the site until the itching ceases, and the pain is soothed; then let the member rest for an hour, then apply a poultice of dry linen, moistened with water or rose oil, and bind it on a nut, until you are sure of the hot abscess; and the inflammation of the member subsides, and the pain is removed, then begin the binding gently again, and a little of the ointment, and do not tighten it as much as before; and gently until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is hot and red and painful and swollen, and you need ointment and bandages, then restart it, just as you did before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.
