If the limb does not receive anything from what we have said, do not dislodge it for three, four, five or seven days; and sometimes leave it for twenty days, depending on what one sees, until the fracture heals and the bone approaches the flesh; then restrain it more than before, and increase its meat, as I have said before; and if you see the site drier than necessary, know that nourishment cannot come to it; wet it therefore with warm water every time you dislodge it, and do this every third day, and loosen a little the bandage; by this action, nourishment comes to the limb, and it improves quickly what the foolish do, who restore the limb crookedly: this is bad, and it is a fearful action, and I see nothing in it but weariness and doing it correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	of the various ways of breaking
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	There are many types of fractures, with distinct causes and appearances. Some fractures are caused by the impact of a sword, breaking the bone all the way to the socket, as with an axe or club; this type of fracture is called a "haichure".
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword cuts the bone without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "surface fracture"; and the wound from these two fractures can be large or small.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a concussive impact, or a cleaving or collar-bone fracture from stone, or from falling on stone, or other similar injuries.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a penetrating fracture which approaches the membrane under the bone, or it is on top of the bone; and this wound is either large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if the wound is repented in the bone as thin as a hair, and the crack is small, then this type of fracture is called  "capillary". If the wound is made by stone, or by falling, or by a similar object, and the bone piece goes inward, and the site is smooth like the blacksmiths when they work on pots; then the bone piece goes inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this happens more often in people with soft bone tissue at the top of the skull, like children's skulls; and it happens to all types of fractures that small pieces are dislocated, as I will explain later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know all kinds of fractures by the distraction over them, and the interrogation under a tent, and through the corruption of the flesh that is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hairline fracture is discovered when one uncovers the bone and rubs it, and a black line appears.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of fractures, be careful of bad omens from the patient, and if you see any harmful signs, such as vomiting blood, loss of consciousness, swelling, fever, eyes popping out, or similar signs in various conditions, then they cannot heal without a doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you don't see any frightening signs and you hope for a cure, then begin the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the newborn comes to you first, and it is winter, you should remove the foreskin before the fourteenth day when you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in the spring, you should remove the foreskin before the seventh day so that the skin under the foreskin does not rot and the complications we have mentioned arise.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes to the membrane that covers the brain, then you should split the split part thus: and it is that you grasp the head of the injured person, and expose the bone in every way you can, and over the wound more gently than you can, and if bleeding occurs when exposing the bone, or if an abscess forms, use the aid that is appropriate. Then fill the area with soft rags soaked in rosemary oil; and let the wound rest until the abscesses are soothed and bleeding stopped; then begin around the bone to remove, and it is done according to two ways of doing: one way is to cut tightly before, and that is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then [you cut] another slit larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have various cuts, some narrow and some wide, and they are pointed and made of iron; and work gently so that you do not bleeding the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is thick and hard, you must pierce it all around, so that you apply cuts with chisels, not so deep that they go through the bone, and you should have a rim or circle on top, preventing the point from going through the bone; and you should have several of these, so that each one comes in the thickness of the bone, so that you have chisels for all parts of the head. And this is the shape of the 3 types of chisels:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing around the broken bone are that you place a probe on the bone and move it with your fingers until you know the bone is pierced; then move the probe elsewhere a little later, and do this all around; then cut into the space between the bones with your incision tools as subtly and lightly as you can, as we have said, until you draw the bone to your hand, or with one of the instruments you have, like tweezers or pincers; and be careful not to touch the brain or the sinus.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have pierced and split the bone, it is fitting that you remove the sharpness that remains on the bone with any other tool resembling a chisel, but it should be more blunt and more delicate than the other chisels; and if anything of the small bones or scales remain, lightly remove them with one of these tools; then cure the wound with tenting and ointments as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment, which Galen describes and highly recommends, is as follows:
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	First you must uncover a part of the bone where the fracture is open, so that when you have uncovered that part, you place under it the head of this lens-shaped instrument, which has this shape.
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	Do not cut from one side only, as the tendon is underneath the bone in two places, so that the cutting is towards the bone; then gently tap with a small mallet, so that you lightly strike the bone all around, and be careful of the tendon which is underneath. If it is stuck to the bone, gently loosen it, for it can be loosened without harm, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the fracture of the bone does not pierce all the way to the membrane, and it is only cut slightly on top, and there are small pieces, then one must smooth out that roughness, and remove the scales with a very subtle rasp; one must have various sizes according to the work and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you use a large razor at first, then one that is more delicate, and do not stop doing this until it is good.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other hair-cutting and shaving techniques, you must adapt to the individual, and this is something that cannot be taught to one who has not devoted themselves to this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the ulcer is exposed, you should take a piece of linen according to the size of the wound, and moisten it in rose oil, and place it over the wound; then take another piece of linen folded in two or three times, and moisten it in wine and rose oil, and place it over the first piece of linen; and do this as gently as you can, so that you do not put too much pressure on the ulcer, then apply another bandage above, without tightening it more than is necessary to hold the wound; and leave it like this for one or two days, until the abscesses are soothed, then loosen it, and apply medicines such as lilium roots, and wheat flour, and incense powder, and aristologus, and similar things; and from these things make a powder, and apply it to the wound, and then apply other medicines without biting; and guard that the wound is clean, so that you do not leave the ointment on it, nor allow any pus to gather, for when pus gathers above the membrane of the brain, it hardens and ruptures, and causes great harm to the patient; for when something biting is applied to the ulcer, it softens from above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Take care therefore, if any bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, without a doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackness does not come, but only because of the medicine that one has applied to it, may such a virtue have, then you should take some honey, and three parts of rose oil and glue a piece of cloth, and put it on the ulcer; then heal it in ways that are appropriate, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that sometimes the two parts of the nose are broken, one only, for there are two bones; and below is cartilage, which does not break, but only swells or becomes dislocated, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, then you should boil your little finger or toe, and put the break inside your index finger, and the poultice with force, until the nail returns according to its natural shape; and do this gently, and be careful that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if the fracture is in the part above the teeth, and the jaw cannot reach its place, then you should put it equal to the head of a rather thick rod.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is on both sides, then do the same thing, and try to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscesses are resolved, then boil at the top of the nail a tent of linen cloth, if the break is in one part.And if the break is on both sides, then do the same thing, and try to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or tenth day, when the abscesses are resolved, then boil at the top of the nail a tent of linen cloth, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you attach one to another side, if the fracture is there; and let the tenters be so thick that they fill the holes of the jaw.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And some restorers say that one must wet the bandages with butter, and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It doesn't seem right to me, but one should wet the bandages in egg white and flour paste; then leave the bandage until the bone is set and the cartilage hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And sometimes feathers of geese are put in place of bandages, and over this a silk cloth is wound around, and the fracture is bound tightly, and the patient breathes through it; now do as you will.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if hot abscesses come to the ears while you are working there, then put cerate or cotton soaked in rose oil, or a poultice of diaquilone.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if a hard abscess comes, then apply a poultice of honey and flour, and incense powder, mixed with egg white; then put over it light wool pads, and do not tie the bandage; and if the fracture in the bone is small, and it is broken into small pieces, extract it with appropriate instruments, then cut the wound, and cure it with warm things, and binding, as with poultices and ointments appropriate to this purpose; and if there is no wound inside the nose, then cure it with bandages, and put in splints of wood, until it is healed.
de la routure de la mandibule	Regarding the dislocation of the jaw:
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is dislocated beneath and there is no external wound, and the dislocation is only slight without any fracture, they can be recognized easily.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is on the right side, to put your left index finger into the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is on the left jaw, put your right index finger, and gently push the fracture inside, and make it even with the other hand by force.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the jaw is displaced in [one of two places], then you must administer extension in one part, so that it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement of the teeth, or splitting, then they must be restrained with a thread of gold or silver or silk; then put a cerote on the broken jaw, and place upon it a double piece of cloth; and upon the cloth, place a large well-made splint, or a piece of leather of equal length and width according to the jaw, and bind it in place as tightly as you can; and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	And if you see that the shape is changing, then loosen it on the third day, and then put back into place what has changed; and apply a poultice over it, made of powdered millstone with an abundance of egg or flour of salsify, after you have removed the cerote; and upon the poultice, apply a thin layer of lamb's wool, and if the poultices become soiled, and the condition of the patient does not change, leave it as long as it takes for him to recover; many times recovery takes place within three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if hot abscesses arise, then administer what we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a break and wound together, examine whether any piece of bone has been removed; then remove it subtly with suitable instruments for this purpose.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it with flame according to your need.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have removed all these pieces, and there remains none, then sew up the wound, if it is wide, and place upon it suitable poultices to encourage scabs, until it is healed.
de la forcele	of the forceps
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The forceps breaks in several ways in front of the shoulder, and the break is according to three patterns: it can be broken and separated into two pieces, which is the easiest to restore; or there can be a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the procedure is as follows when the break is without a wound: you need two assistants, one of whom holds the shoulder where the forceps are broken, and the other stretches the neck towards the affected part; then, with your fingers, bring the broken pieces together so that the joint is in the correct position, with no visible gap or misalignment.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	If you need to extend the joint further, place a round pillow of cloth or fabric under the shoulder, and make it as thick as necessary; then release the forceps and hold the pillow in your hand, bringing the broken pieces together so that they are aligned correctly.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the shoulder out of its socket because it comes in deeply, then the patient should lie on his back, and put one ear to the ground, and the minister should push the shoulder down while lifting the bone of the shoulder.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then you should apply the fracture with your fingers, and if you find it broken, then you must split it; gently pull out the pieces, and if the bone cannot join because of an overgrowth, then cut it at one of the incisions you have made; but put this instrument under the shoulder to ward off the syphilis:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	It should be the size of a spoon, not shaved down, and as wide as is necessary according to the size of the bone and the extent of the work; it has two heads, as you can see, one wide and the other narrow, like the path of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are sure of the hot abscess, cut open the wound, and if the path is small or you doubt the hot abscess, then close the wound with bandages and tents according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if there are deep abscesses, moisten a cloth in rose oil and vinegar and wine, and apply it.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The dislocation of the bone, when there is no wound or fracture, is to put on the bone the plaster made from mill powder and egg white, and place light sponges on top, and if necessary, put a splint under the sore; then take a very wide band, about a palm's width, and place two layers of cloth over the sponges and plaster; then take a slender rod, three fingers in width and length, and wrap it around the band so that the ends of the band hang down; and place the rod on the fracture, and wrap the band around the neck, and under the healthy shoulder blade, and under the sore shoulder blade; and adjust each part, and when you see that the ligament holds the fracture in alignment, and you clearly see that the rod is not moving over the broken bone, then re-bandage it every day, and when the ligament loosens, restrain it; and have the patient lie on his back, and place a small pillow under the shoulder blade while he sleeps, to raise the shoulder; thus the dislocation will be healed by the alignment of the shoulder joint, or tie the arm to the neck, and do not untie it if an evil accident does not occur, until the twentieth day; then start the plaster again, if you see that it is needed, and adjust it thus, until it is healed; and it is usually healed within twenty-eight days, and less for some people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	from the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	It happens that the shoulder is broken or widely displaced, and it is not set except by touch; then shape the apparatus according to the pattern of the break, and reset it according to its natural form, in every way you can; then put powdered flour from the mill with plenty of egg white over the area, and apply light poultices, and place a double layer of cloth over them; then place a large and thin plaster over the shoulder, slightly larger than the shoulder itself, and if there is a swelling underneath the plaster anywhere on the shoulder, fill that hollow with a poultice of linen until the plaster sits level; then hold it firmly in place with a large bandage, so that the plaster does not move from its position, and check the bandage every day; whenever it becomes loose, tighten it again, and if the plaster is displaced, adjust it to its proper position, and let the patient lie on his side; the shoulder will be restored within 20 or 25 days. And when this period is complete, remove the bandage, and be confident, for this is not a bone that sets easily.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone protrudes forward, and not under the heart, they should cut it off, and the bone, and do what we have said about relieving the hot abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	from the break in the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The penis is sometimes broken in the middle, but this happens rarely; it more often breaks at the tip.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when it is broken in the middle, it bends downward, and the patient feels great pain, and loses urine, and is constipated, and perhaps vomits blood, and the hair grows on the broken bone, and he feels little good.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is for the patient to lie on his back, and place a pillow between his shoulders, then press the shoulders together and bring the ribs close together with his hands, making sure that the bones are in their proper position; then he should apply plasters and bandages over the broken bone, using salt or some other light material, and wrap it in a cloth, binding it firmly to the bone so that it does not move; then he should bind the linen tightly around the waist, and every hour loosen the binding, and if it softens, tighten it again; and if it needs to be loosed for corrosion or itching that comes to the area, or pain or abscess, then he should hurry and loosen it, and wash away what has come out from the wound, and dress it according to the various methods of treatment; then re-apply the plaster, and tighten it until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the fracture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Know that rib fractures occur only in the large ribs near the back, and in the upper part inside, and they bend only because they are slippery; and one feels it well on examination at both ends.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And the treatment is that you set the break evenly as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	Then apply the ointment and bind it with a bandage if necessary.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rib fracture is bent inward, then the patient feels great pain and piercing, as with pleurisy, for the bone punctures the lining; and he has difficulty breathing, and coughs up a great quantity of blood, and it is a serious illness, and the ancient physicians placed great importance on it.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if one has a fracture, they say that one should eat foods that bloat the belly, to force out the broken bone.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not make hot poultices unless an abscess is already there.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if it is there, then we cleanse it.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And some say that one should place leeches on the site to draw out pus, and this is reasonable; however, there is a risk that the leech will attract excess fluids due to the weakness of the patient.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And some say that one should cover the place with soft wool soaked in hot oil, and put tents between the ribs to make the area around even, then it should be bandaged with a bandage of pleurisy, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot endure because of the bone that points through the bandage, and there is doubt about the patient, then one should split above the broken rib, and put an instrument underneath to ward off the syphilis; then one must cut the bone and pull gently, and then sew up the two lips of the wound if it is large, and dress the wound with ointments until it heals.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the hot abscesses come, then put on wet clothes in rosemary oil, and put it on the spot; and cure the area around the abscess as needed, and let him lie still on his side where he should, until he is healed.
de la brisure dou col	about the fracture of the neck:
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Sometimes there is a break in the bones of the neck, and it can bend; and also in the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this happens to someone, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, take note if you see his hands soft, swollen, and numb, and he cannot move them or stretch them, and when you prick him with a needle, he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is deadly in many cases, and if he moves his hands and feels the pain when you dislocate them and press on them, know that the joint of the bone is safe, and that the disease is healed if you apply a cure to it.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if a similar condition occurs in the spine of the back, and you want to know if he will be healed or not, take note if his feet are numb, and if the symptoms are in his hands, and there is vomiting and diarrhea without volition; and when he lies on his stomach, there is also diarrhea without volition.Et si li accident i sont en la cief, et tu vuoils savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si luy fay sovinir sus ses piez, et met li piez dous draps moilliez, et luy fay boire vin de venie; et quant il a esteit sovineit, si luy fay boire un peu de vin, et quant il s’est traicteit, si prend li piez et les remue, et li dis que li piez sont moilliez.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when he is laying on his back and he wants to sit up, he cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	You should know that it is deadly; therefore do not labor over its treatment.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if these signs do not occur, the condition is more mild.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the treatment is that you apply a hot poultice to the spine if there is an abscess, using rose oil or egg yolk oil until it is soothed; then apply one of the comforting and drying poultices, and bind it with a bandage, and command the patient to rest; and let him not sleep on the part where he feels pain until he is healed.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if any bone is dislocated, one should cover it with the palm of one's hand; and remove the bone, then join the two lips of the wound, if it is large, with a single stitch, then treat the wound with ointment until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the 'head of the cow', put your thumb in your left hand, and place it equally in your right hand, then apply the plaster and bandage on top, if you need to; then bind it tightly, and if there are bones dislocated, do the same, then remove them, and treat the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	of the fracture of the hip bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	Sometimes the hip bone is fractured, and if it does, there will be a slight shrinking at the head; and it will bend to one side, and the patient feels pain in that spot, and there will be a point and swelling where it is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And its restoration is that you extend your hand over it, so that you are on the fracture; and you know which is the fracture and the shape of it; and if the fracture is only at the head, then put that fracture in line with the rest of the bone so that it is in a natural shape.Et si la brisure est au pardedens soulement, si met cele sus le chief tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it inclines inward, then have the patient lie on his stomach until the setting of that fracture is prepared.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set it straight, then apply the plaster, and then place a wooden or leather splint on top, and bind the fracture so that it does not move; and apply the linen under the rib cage until the fracture is healed.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his healthy side or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if painful bumps appear, do not touch them until the painful bumps are soothed, and apply what we have described earlier; then return to the healing process, and bind it as it should be, if there is no bad outcome; and that is the method.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The adjutoires is that which is between the neck and the head of the shoulder; and if it is broken, one should restore it according to one of two methods. The first is that you take a rod straight and smooth, according to this form:
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And tie the two ends with ropes and raise them up, and seat the patient on a chair; then let him gently hang his broken arm over the rod, until it comes to rest, and have a curve in the rod, then let him lean back onto something heavy or let his ministers hold him down; then let his assistants bring the broken joint together as evenly as possible, so that the joint returns to its proper place.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And the other method is that one supports the patient on his back, and ties his hand to his neck, then let one minister hold what is above the break in his hands, and the other minister hold below at the end of the rod, and each pulls their respective ends.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more difficult, then press the ligament below the fracture and above it, and stretch each of the ministers to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the head of the shoulder, you should place one ligament in the middle of the dislocation and another towards the neck under the fracture; and likewise, if the fracture is towards the neck, then gently place a ligament without exertion, so that the fracture remains even under the shoulder and the neck; then even out the fracture as it should be, and bind it, if no abscesses appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if hot abscesses come, do not tighten it for 7 days; then put cool linen in vinegar and rose oil on the hot abscesses until they are soothed; then tighten it, and the manner of tightening is that you put the plaster on the fracture, then raise the arm onto the shoulder, and place your hand on the shoulder or breast; and put a cloth, and press onto the shoulder and the arm so that the arm is in its natural place, unless something keeps it from being so, or if the bone is displaced.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is moving, use splints, and put a wider and stronger splint on the fracture, with a space of two fingers between each splint, and let each splint be as long so that it passes the fracture by three inches on each side; then tighten onto the splints as I said at the beginning of the chapter, more firmly and less in moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see that the bones are settled and bound as we have said, during the hour that you restore the broken member, and you suspect a hot abscess, then leave it bound until the seventh day as we have said; then examine the bandage every third day so that itching or swelling does not occur at the site, or that the nutrients cannot reach the member because it is too tight.Et se li prurite ou enflement viegne, si doit tu deffaire li membre, et le lavere en ches k’il est estrois et asserate, et li membredre apes le leu luisant; puis le laisse secher et remets liien sanz liier, si com il est igal.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If it dislocates, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accidents occur, then do not release it until three days or more have passed, and let the patient sleep on his back, and place his hands on his stomach; and put underneath the shoulder a pillow filled with wool of equal thickness, and check every hour during the day or night that the dislocated member does not move, or soften the ligaments; then release it using medicine, and give him the food we mentioned earlier, in such a way that the food is very subtle at first; and when he begins to recover, make it thicker.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is customary for the shoulder and leg to be reset after 40 days of healing; then one should release it and administer baths and ointments to encourage healing.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stricture is bad and blocked, it will remain for days or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the breaking of the arm
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "bone-pair"; one is small and lies beneath the armpit, and the other is large and lies beneath the small bone; sometimes only the large bone breaks, or the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are broken, their restoration is easy and healing quick; but when the large bones are broken, healing is more difficult, and it takes longer than when they are only bruised.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If it is only the small bone that is broken, then it should be extended gently and placed evenly.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large bone, then it should be pulled more forcefully; and he should lie on his back, with his affected arm raised above the others, and his small fingers lower than the other fingers, and he should cross his legs over his chest, and the pillow under his head for support so that he does not struggle; then the assistant should raise the unaffected arm up towards the affected hand, or towards the elbow, and another assistant should push down on the arm above the affected one.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then let him examine it evenly, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the breaking there are pieces, one places each in its place, and if there is any dislocation that pinches the heart, and you cannot restore it to its place, then split it along the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the fracture there is a wound, I have spoken singularly about it in this chapter; then take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the healing there are hot abscesses, apply a poultice made from rosemary oil and white wax, neither too hard nor too soft; and place the poultice gently on top, until the hot abscesses are soothed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then remove the cerote, and apply the plaster made from mill-powder with beaten egg, then place the splints, and let the splint of the fracture be slightly larger and stronger; and let there be six splints on the arm in various positions: whether the fracture is in one bone or two; and tighten more over the fracture than elsewhere, lessening the tightness as it heals, as I have said at the beginning of this chapter. Let the linen underneath be soft and moist, not hard or rough; and let the string used to tighten the splints be made of flax, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And then examine the member and the ligament after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any bad accident happens to the member, such as itching coming to the member, then you should wet the member with warm water until those itches are relieved; and let the member not be tightly bound but rest.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then restart the binding, and if the ligaments are softened and the bones separated, and similar things, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if you see that the nourishment cannot come to the member because it is too bound, then you must soften it a little, and leave it thus for several days, until the nourishment runs to it, and then tighten it again.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said come to the patient, then do not release him until 20 days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Or if in what we have said there is no improvement for the patient, then he can use his hands around his neck and his neck should be even, and he should guard against movement and shaking, and sleep on his back; and know that this fracture will be healed in 30 days or 35 at most, and perhaps in 20 days according to the compositions and complexes of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the fracture of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Know that in the back of the hand and around the fingers there are few fractures, and they only come from bending many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the palm of the hand is broken or bent, then the patient should stretch his arm out straight in front of him evenly; then he should put his hand on the ground, and stretch out the broken bones, and put them back together evenly, the minister, as far as the injury extends; and if there are no abscesses, then put on a plaster and bandages; then wrap it in a single linen cloth.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is in the peritoneum around the abdomen of the plant, make a bandage of rags, and instruct the patient to press it against his broken plant; then squeeze it with a long strip of cloth, and let the mark of the finger be as large as the palm of the hand, and squeeze it as it should be.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the fracture is in the arm, you must put a splint on top and another underneath in the plant, so that the hand is open and straight, then bind it all around the hand and stop the bleeding between the fingers.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the fracture is in one of the fingers, if it's the thumb, set it straight as it should be and then squeeze the hand, and if you see fit, put a small straight splint to raise the fracture and keep it from moving; and if the fracture is in any other finger, such as the index or another, set it straight and bind it with the finger next to it; or bind them all together while holding it steady, or you can put a splint on top of the finger like a thumb; take care in the restoration and treatment of a hot abscess, and treat any pus that arises as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken thigh
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the thigh are often broken, and one can see this when they bend forward and backward; and their healing is by binding one band above the fracture, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And let the patient lie on his face, then extend each band equally to their respective parts; and this is how it is done when the fracture is within the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is close to the root of the thigh, let one ligature be towards the armpit and the other ligature below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And likewise if it is near the knee, let the ligature be beyond the knee, and let the extension be below; then the surgeon puts his fingers on the bone, making it equal to his two hands, until it is according to its natural figure, and then put on the plaster, and the bandage, if no abscess comes out.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if the patient has a hot abscess, then let it subside and then return to your treatment and care; the bandage is done in the following way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	You should wrap a folded bandage two or three times around the fracture, and leave the excess, then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the thigh, and tie a long thread between the thigh and the leg beyond the knee, and bring the ends of the thread up above; then go back over the leg and the thigh with the bandage, then put splints on the fracture, and put one splint on the bone of the leg; then press the area firmly between the leg and the thigh with soft pieces of cloth to even out the pressure, then start binding the fracture firmly three or four times; and the more you go up from the fracture, the less you should bind it; then tie the two ends of the thread which you have put through between the leg and the thigh, then put on three splints that are above, then go back to below the end of the thread, so that you come to the foot; and bind it, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it thus, so that no abscess or swelling or anything similar comes.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if something happens, then loosen it and adjust what has happened, as we have said many times before; and if there are pieces of bone that are poking out, they should be removed if possible; if not, the area should be split open and drained, and the wound treated as we have described, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	Sometimes the thigh is broken like this when splints are put on, as in the shoulder and arm; nevertheless, when restored in this way, it does not harm the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And you should know that the neck is restored within a day, or less or more, depending on the different complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groove of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Know that in the knee joint there is little breaking, but it bends many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, it is only a split, or a hole, and it happens with all wounds, whether with or without pain, and everyone feels it.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is to put it back in place with tweezers, as long as he can; then put on the ointment, and if necessary, put a round splint, and bind it as it should be, then follow all the instructions that we have given for other fractures, such as a hot abscess and similar; then treat each incident as appropriate, until it is healed.
de la brisure de la jambe	of the fracture of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Know that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called by right name 'mustelz', and the other is called 'foscile'; and all injuries occur as they do in the arm, and so its restoration is the same, and the works are all the same. And if both bones are broken together, then the leg turns over entirely.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if only the smaller bones are broken, then it turns forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, one feels great pain, and one sees it well; and it turns underneath.Et s’il est brisiez li osses petits, si ne sent on pas dolor, et ne le voit on pas; et est tout auteil si com cele dou bras igalment.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore bring about an extension, and make it even, and tie the bones evenly; but nevertheless, if the fracture is ugly, and there are several pieces, then the extension should be less and lighter; and adjust according to your ability.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have finished your work, then take two wooden splints that prop up the leg on either side, and let them be as long as from the knee to below; then wrap two bands above and below, and tie it in the middle also, and at this time the leg will not decline to the right or left, and so it is well; and some administer a board as long as the leg, made of wood, and they put the leg upon it to guard against movement, and properly do they treat that in the fracture where there is pain; and move the leg every day to see if there is any hot abscess or other accident; and cure it until it is healed.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of bone fracture at the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no fracture, but sometimes there is a bone fracture at the foot and in two ways, and there is no more force than that in many positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in the bone of the foot, and you see the bones on top of one another, then put the foot of the patient on the ground, as if he wanted to walk, and then put your own foot on top of his, where the bones are raised, then press down until they return to their places; then apply the ointment and bandages on top, and place a small wooden board with two flat sides underneath the belly of the foot, then bind it to the foot securely, and then wrap cloth and other materials around it as needed.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And after three or four days have passed, loosen the binding, for you will find the bones healed, whether broken or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	And if there is a broken bone in the toe, then set it as we have said for the fingers of the hand; then place a splint along the length of the toe, and let it be slightly wider, then place underneath the foot that small board I mentioned earlier, and tighten it securely; and if there are one or two, or more, broken bones, then place a splint on each toe according to its size, wrapped in one piece of linen, and tighten the board underneath the foot; and let the top of the board press firmly against the belly of the foot.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And you must not forget the other things that I have said about other fractures, from what we have already discussed; and treat each incident as it should be treated.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	from the fracture of the bone in the shoulder
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of a woman is broken, make her sit with her hips widened, then tilt her towards her back, and have her held from behind; then fill the wound with cotton, and place as many pebbles inside as there are bones; then help the woman to stand up, and gently loosen her back little by little, and thus the pebbles and cotton will come out as they enter the wound, and the bone will return to its place with them; and when she wants to urinate, remove the cotton, and when she has urinated, put it back in, and do this for seven days; then the fracture will be restored. Take a lamb's bladder, attach a cane to the opening, fill the bladder inside the wound; then blow into the cane forcefully, until the bladder is inflated inside: the bone will return to its place; then fill it with cotton, and leave it like that for a few days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the bone of the elbow of a man or woman is broken, restore it as we have said for the bone of the hip; and these breaks are not hidden from him who applies his study and understanding to my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the breaks indicate in many ways the right path to restoration: understand it therefore.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	For a broken penis, take a goose's gullet and insert it into the penis; then wrap it with cloth and leave it for three days, checking on it daily, and it will be healed quickly.
de brisure avec plaie	of fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	One who has a fracture with a wound, especially if it is large, like the fracture of the thigh or shoulder or similar, should be treated now, as the bleeding we have described attests.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound bleeds, then resume reducing the fracture in that same hour or that day, if no abscesses appear.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if abscesses appear, then leave the reduction until the next day, waiting for the abscesses to subside; do not touch or treat them on the third or fourth day, for you would risk causing a harmful incident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is visible on the uncovered chest, then you should gently put it in place with your hands, with a small extension.
